Assistant: Understood. With “edge lengths shall remain constant” and paw lift amplitude allowed to be 0, **Running 0 can be made extremely simple and internally consistent**:

## Running 0 definition (Mouse 1.0)

### Parameters
- Let `z_head` be the **rest-pose local z-coordinate** of the `head` node (since your reference point is at `(0,0,0)` on the local ground plane).
- **Stride length**
  - `stride_len = z_head / 3`
  - In Mouse 1.0 this can be recorded/derived but **does not need to be used** if paws don’t animate.

### Pose during running
- **No internal articulation at all**:
  - For every node `i`: `p_i_local(t) = p_i0` (the rest pose from the file)
- Consequently:
  - **All edge lengths remain constant** automatically (the entire skeleton is a rigid shape in local space).
  - Ears–nose triangle remains rigid automatically.

### World motion during running
- The only motion is the rigid-body transform from the track generator:
  - Translation `P(t) = (x(t), y(t), 0)`
  - Yaw rotation `Rz(θ(t))`
- World coordinates:
  - `p_i_world(t) = P(t) + Rz(θ(t)) * p_i0`

That’s it. The mouse “runs” by moving through the cage, but the skeleton pose stays fixed.

This is consistent with your stated goal: **simple simulation > physical plausibility**.

---

## Important consequence for rearing (given constant edge lengths)
Because you require edge lengths to remain constant, any rearing pose changes must be implemented as **rotations around joints** (forward kinematics) or as a rigid-body rotation of the whole skeleton — but **not** by “clamping paws to z=0” after the fact, because that would generally change bone lengths.

So for rearing, we’ll define it as:
- either a **whole-body pitch** around a chosen pivot (e.g., around the hind paws midpoint or tail root), or
- a **jointed pitch** at `tail_root` (and maybe at `head`) propagated through the tree.

Both preserve all edge lengths exactly.

---

## Recording outputs (fits Running 0 now)
Since node positions come from a rigid transform, recording is clean:

- **3D ground truth per frame**: `time, behavior, node_label, x, y, z`
- **2D keypoints per camera per frame**: `time, behavior, camera_id, node_label, u, v, visible`

And the video is just visualization.

---

If you now specify **Rearing 1** in the same “as-simple-as-possible” spirit, I’ll lock it into an equally strict definition that preserves edge lengths (no hacks), and then we can move directly into coding the simulator + camera projections + file/video output.

User: The running behavior needs to be a bit more dynamic than you described it last: we need to keep the trot motion of the paws. Just sliding a rigid model through global space is not sufficient . In addition to that we need the trot pattern of the paws. In straight forward motion this means that while e.g. left front and right hind paw are fixed to the ground the opposite paws (right front and left hind paws move twice as fast forwards as the model (coordinate system) in global space. Only if the path is curved (and that is what I wanted to say earlier) the simplicity of ground fixed and moving paws would be gone. Which is why I said the formally fixed paws will be allowed not to be fixed due to the curvedness of the path.

Assistant: You’re trying to combine three requirements that, with your **current graph**, can’t all be true at the same time:

1) **Front paw is a node connected directly to `head` by a single edge (a rigid “bone”)**  
2) **Edge lengths remain constant**  
3) **During trot, a paw can stay fixed on the ground (z=0) while the body advances**

With a **single rigid segment** `head → front_paw`, if the paw is on the ground (`z=0`) then (in the simplest sagittal-plane view) the paw is confined to a **circle** around the head. If you also insist the paw is fixed in world coordinates while the head moves forward, the distance from head to paw will generally change — violating constant edge length. In other words: **a one-bone leg cannot do stance-phase ground fixation with forward body motion**.

So you have to relax *one* thing. The good news is: there are two clean, minimal ways forward.

---

## Option A (no graph change): keep trot timing, drop “fixed to ground”
This is the simplest “Mouse 1.0” approach and matches what you said about allowing non-fixed paws due to curvature. It also respects **constant edge lengths** (because paws are moved by *rotating* around their parent).

### What you can do with one-edge legs
You can still do a visually trot-like pattern by driving each paw on an **arc** (distance to parent fixed):

- Front paws move on arcs around `head`
- Hind paws move on arcs around `tail_root`

Define trot phase `φ(t)` (tied to speed as before), and set diagonal pairing:

- Pair A (stance when `sin φ > 0`): `LFP + RHP`
- Pair B (stance when `sin(φ+π) > 0`): `RFP + LHP`

Then for each paw, define an **angle** that swings forward/back:

- `α_swing(t) = α0 + Aα * sin(φ + phase_offset)`
- paw local position is computed by rotating the rest vector about the local **y-axis** (forward/up plane), keeping length constant:
  - `p_paw_local(t) = p_parent0 + Ry(α_swing(t)) * (p_paw0 - p_parent0)`

This guarantees constant edge lengths exactly and produces “trot timing” (diagonal pairs moving oppositely).  
What it does **not** guarantee is foot contact with the ground during stance, because with one segment you can’t enforce that.

You can *suggest* contact by choosing the arc so the paw is near `z≈0` for part of the cycle, but it won’t be exact.

This is the “cheap-but-consistent” Mouse 1.0 solution.

---

## Option B (minimal graph change): add one intermediate joint per leg and you *can* do stance fixation
If you truly want: “paw fixed in world during stance; swing paw moves forward faster than body”, **and** constant edge lengths, then you need at least a **two-link leg**.

Minimal additions:

- `left_shoulder`, `right_shoulder` between `head` and each front paw  
  edges: `head–left_shoulder–left_front_paw`, `head–right_shoulder–right_front_paw`
- `left_hip`, `right_hip` between `tail_root` and each hind paw  
  edges: `tail_root–left_hip–left_hind_paw`, `tail_root–right_hip–right_hind_paw`

That’s 4 extra nodes and 4 extra edges. Still simple, but now each leg is 2 segments with fixed lengths.

### How trot works then (cleanly)
Per time step, you do:

1) **Update body rigid motion** along the path: `P(t), θ(t)`  
   (same as before)

2) **Decide gait phase** (trot):
   - stance legs: foot target stays constant in world
   - swing legs: foot target advances

3) **Foot target update**
   - For each stance paw: keep `F_world` unchanged (or very small slip allowed)
   - For each swing paw: move it forward in the *body-forward direction* on the ground:
     - simplest version matching your statement:
       - swing forward speed = `2 * v_body`
       - so `F_world += (2*v_body*dt) * forward_dir_xy`  
     This produces the “twice as fast as the model” effect in straight motion.

   When the path curves, “true fixed stance” is still achievable with 2-link legs as long as the target remains within reachable workspace; if not, you allow slip (small correction).

4) **Solve 2-link IK in a plane** for each leg
For each leg you know:
- hip/shoulder world point `H_world` (derived from body transform)
- desired foot world point `F_world` (on z=0)
- segment lengths `L1, L2` from the mouse file (rest lengths)

Solve planar 2-link IK in the sagittal plane defined by forward axis and up axis (or directly in 3D by reducing to a plane). This yields knee/elbow position and therefore joint angles; you then compute local node positions and transform to world.

This enforces:
- paw fixed during stance (exactly, if reachable)
- constant edge lengths (exactly)
- swing motion speed rule (exactly, because it’s in the foot target update)

---

## Which option fits “Mouse 1.0” best?
- If you want **no file format changes**: Option A. You’ll get trot *timing* and visible limb motion, but not true stance fixation.
- If you want the *specific* “stance fixed, swing twice speed” statement to be **actually true** under constant edge lengths: Option B, with 4 added nodes and simple 2-link IK.

Given your new requirement, Option B is the minimal way to make the model logically consistent.

---

## Practical proposal (so you can simulate now)
Do this in Mouse 1.0 without overengineering:

1) Implement Option A immediately (rotational arc trot) so you get end-to-end working: track → pose → cameras → 3D+2D recording.
2) Add Option B as a small “graph v2” later (still Mouse 1.0), because it only changes the skeleton file and adds a small IK solver.

If you want, I can write the exact mouse.txt format for Option B (nodes + edges + rest lengths implied), plus the precise trot state machine (stance/swing timing, foot target initialization, and IK equations) in a way that drops directly into code.

User: Yes , please code option A. I understand that the arc length constraint cannot be enforced. Lets rather assume that the paw moves parallel to the symmetry plane at z=0. Please follow (or also follow) your suggestions above with a reasonable compromise.

Assistant: ```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Mouse 1.0 — Option A (simple trot, no strict leg kinematics)

- Reads a mouse skeleton tree from a text file (nodes + edges).
- Simulates a random 2D track in a rectangular cage on z=0 with smooth heading changes.
- Behaviors:
    0 = running (trot gait on ground plane z=0, paws move in local x only; diagonal pairing)
    1 = rearing (very simple placeholder: pitch body up/down, lift front paws; can be refined later)
- 3 orthogonal cameras (top/front/side) produce:
    - mp4 videos (if possible)
    - exact 2D projections (keypoints) without noise
- Saves 3D ground-truth coordinates per frame.

Key compromises (as requested):
- Paws move parallel to symmetry plane and stay on z=0 (no paw lift by default).
- This changes head–paw and tailroot–hindpaw edge lengths; head–ears–nose triangle stays rigid.
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
import csv
import math
import os
import random
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np

# Optional video backend
_VIDEO_BACKEND = None
try:
    import cv2  # type: ignore
    _VIDEO_BACKEND = "opencv"
except Exception:
    cv2 = None  # type: ignore

if _VIDEO_BACKEND is None:
    try:
        import imageio  # type: ignore
        _VIDEO_BACKEND = "imageio"
    except Exception:
        imageio = None  # type: ignore


# ----------------------------
# File parsing (mouse graph)
# ----------------------------

def _norm_label(s: str) -> str:
    return s.strip().lower().replace(" ", "_")


@dataclass
class MouseGraph:
    # local rest pose coords (mouse model coordinate system)
    nodes: Dict[str, np.ndarray]          # label -> (3,)
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]]          # (a,b)
    # node order for output (stable)
    node_order: List[str]

    def require(self, label: str) -> str:
        key = _norm_label(label)
        if key not in self.nodes:
            raise ValueError(f"Mouse graph missing required node: {label}")
        return key


def load_mouse_graph(path: str) -> MouseGraph:
    """
    Minimal, forgiving format:

    [NODES]
    head  0.0 0.0 2.4
    nose_tip  1.2 0.0 2.2
    left_ear_tip 0.2 0.5 2.8
    ...
    [EDGES]
    head nose_tip
    head left_ear_tip
    ...

    Lines starting with # are comments. Empty lines ignored.
    """
    if not os.path.exists(path):
        raise FileNotFoundError(path)

    mode = None
    nodes: Dict[str, np.ndarray] = {}
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]] = []
    node_order: List[str] = []

    with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        for raw in f:
            line = raw.strip()
            if not line or line.startswith("#"):
                continue
            if line.upper() == "[NODES]":
                mode = "nodes"
                continue
            if line.upper() == "[EDGES]":
                mode = "edges"
                continue
            if mode == "nodes":
                parts = line.split()
                if len(parts) != 4:
                    raise ValueError(f"Bad node line: {line}")
                label = _norm_label(parts[0])
                x, y, z = map(float, parts[1:])
                if label in nodes:
                    raise ValueError(f"Duplicate node label: {label}")
                nodes[label] = np.array([x, y, z], dtype=np.float64)
                node_order.append(label)
            elif mode == "edges":
                parts = line.split()
                if len(parts) != 2:
                    raise ValueError(f"Bad edge line: {line}")
                a, b = _norm_label(parts[0]), _norm_label(parts[1])
                edges.append((a, b))
            else:
                raise ValueError(f"File must start with [NODES] section. Got: {line}")

    if not nodes:
        raise ValueError("No nodes loaded.")
    if not edges:
        raise ValueError("No edges loaded.")

    return MouseGraph(nodes=nodes, edges=edges, node_order=node_order)


# ----------------------------
# Math helpers
# ----------------------------

def rotz(theta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    c, s = math.cos(theta), math.sin(theta)
    return np.array([[c, -s, 0.0],
                     [s,  c, 0.0],
                     [0.0, 0.0, 1.0]], dtype=np.float64)

def roty(theta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    c, s = math.cos(theta), math.sin(theta)
    return np.array([[ c, 0.0, s],
                     [0.0, 1.0, 0.0],
                     [-s, 0.0, c]], dtype=np.float64)

def rotx(theta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    c, s = math.cos(theta), math.sin(theta)
    return np.array([[1.0, 0.0, 0.0],
                     [0.0,  c, -s],
                     [0.0,  s,  c]], dtype=np.float64)

def smoothstep01(u: float) -> float:
    u = max(0.0, min(1.0, u))
    return u*u*(3.0 - 2.0*u)


# ----------------------------
# Random track model (smooth heading + speed)
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class TrackState:
    x: float
    y: float
    theta: float   # yaw heading
    v: float       # speed
    omega: float   # yaw rate


def step_track(
    st: TrackState,
    dt: float,
    cage_w: float,
    cage_d: float,
    max_speed: float,
    omega_max: float,
    speed_noise: float,
    omega_noise: float,
    speed_damp: float,
    omega_damp: float,
    wall_repulse_gain: float,
    wall_repulse_dist: float,
    rng: random.Random,
) -> TrackState:
    # OU-ish update
    st.v += (-speed_damp * st.v) * dt + speed_noise * math.sqrt(dt) * rng.gauss(0, 1)
    st.omega += (-omega_damp * st.omega) * dt + omega_noise * math.sqrt(dt) * rng.gauss(0, 1)

    st.v = max(0.0, min(max_speed, st.v))
    st.omega = max(-omega_max, min(omega_max, st.omega))

    # wall repulsion: add steering away from walls (affects omega)
    # Compute distance to each wall
    dL = st.x
    dR = cage_w - st.x
    dB = st.y
    dT = cage_d - st.y
    steer = 0.0

    def repulse(d: float) -> float:
        if d <= 1e-6:
            return 1.0
        if d >= wall_repulse_dist:
            return 0.0
        # stronger when closer
        return (wall_repulse_dist - d) / wall_repulse_dist

    # heuristic: if near left wall, steer right (negative/positive depends on heading)
    # We produce a desired heading to the cage center and blend via omega.
    cx, cy = cage_w * 0.5, cage_d * 0.5
    to_c = math.atan2(cy - st.y, cx - st.x)
    # blend factor based on proximity to any wall
    prox = max(repulse(dL), repulse(dR), repulse(dB), repulse(dT))
    # steering correction: shortest signed angle difference
    def ang_diff(a: float, b: float) -> float:
        d = (a - b + math.pi) % (2*math.pi) - math.pi
        return d
    steer = -wall_repulse_gain * prox * ang_diff(st.theta, to_c)

    st.theta += (st.omega + steer) * dt

    # predict step
    nx = st.x + st.v * dt * math.cos(st.theta)
    ny = st.y + st.v * dt * math.sin(st.theta)

    # reflect at hard boundaries if needed
    if nx < 0.0 or nx > cage_w:
        st.theta = math.pi - st.theta
        nx = min(max(nx, 0.0), cage_w)
    if ny < 0.0 or ny > cage_d:
        st.theta = -st.theta
        ny = min(max(ny, 0.0), cage_d)

    st.x, st.y = nx, ny
    return st


# ----------------------------
# Behaviors
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class BehaviorState:
    behavior: int
    t_in_state: float
    state_duration: float
    # running gait
    gait_phase: float  # radians

def sample_duration(behavior: int, rng: random.Random) -> float:
    # Simple defaults; tweak later
    if behavior == 0:  # running
        return rng.uniform(2.0, 6.0)
    else:              # rearing
        return rng.uniform(0.6, 1.6)

def next_behavior(current: int, rng: random.Random) -> int:
    # Simple: alternate with randomness
    if current == 0:
        return 1 if rng.random() < 0.25 else 0
    else:
        return 0


def pose_running_option_a(
    g: MouseGraph,
    dt: float,
    v_body: float,
    gait_phase: float,
    stride_len: float,
    head_jitter_amp_deg: float,
    head_jitter_hz: float,
    t_global: float,
    rng: random.Random,
) -> Tuple[Dict[str, np.ndarray], float]:
    """
    Running pose:
    - head-ears-nose cluster stays rigid via small rotations around head
    - paws remain on z=0 and move in local x only, with diagonal trot timing.
      Approximate stance: paw x moves backward relative to body during stance,
      and forward during swing; tied to v and stride_len.
    """
    nodes = {k: v.copy() for k, v in g.nodes.items()}

    head = g.require("head")
    nose = g.require("nose_tip")
    le = g.require("left_ear_tip")
    re = g.require("right_ear_tip")
    lfp = g.require("left_front_paw")
    rfp = g.require("right_front_paw")
    lhp = g.require("left_hind_paw")
    rhp = g.require("right_hind_paw")
    tail_root = g.require("tail_root")

    # --- head rigid cluster rotation (small, keeps triangle rigid) ---
    # Use deterministic sinusoids + tiny random drift
    A = math.radians(head_jitter_amp_deg)
    w = 2 * math.pi * head_jitter_hz
    pitch = A * math.sin(w * t_global + 0.3)
    roll  = A * 0.7 * math.sin(w * t_global + 1.1)
    yaw   = A * 0.5 * math.sin(w * t_global + 2.0)

    Q = rotz(yaw) @ rotx(roll) @ roty(pitch)

    head_pos = nodes[head].copy()
    for key in (nose, le, re):
        v0 = g.nodes[key] - g.nodes[head]
        nodes[key] = head_pos + Q @ v0

    # --- trot paw x motion (z=0, y fixed) ---
    # cadence tied to speed: phase advance dφ = 2π*(v/stride_len)*dt
    # avoid division by zero:
    if stride_len <= 1e-9 or v_body <= 1e-9:
        dphi = 0.0
    else:
        dphi = 2 * math.pi * (v_body / stride_len) * dt

    gait_phase = (gait_phase + dphi) % (2 * math.pi)

    # Define triangular wave in [-1,1] from phase, with stance vs swing.
    # We'll use a piecewise linear saw that yields:
    # stance: x decreases by stride_len/2 over half cycle,
    # swing:  x increases by stride_len/2 over half cycle,
    # centered around 0.
    def tri_wave(phase: float) -> float:
        # map phase to [0,1)
        u = (phase % (2*math.pi)) / (2*math.pi)
        # triangle wave 0..1..0
        if u < 0.5:
            return 1.0 - 4.0*u  # 1 -> -1 over [0,0.5)
        else:
            return -3.0 + 4.0*u # -1 -> 1 over [0.5,1)
    # tri_wave returns +1 at start stance, -1 at end stance, +1 at end swing

    # diagonal pairing offsets:
    # Pair A in stance when phase ~0..π (tri wave decreasing)
    # Pair B is shifted by π
    def paw_x_offset(phase: float) -> float:
        # amplitude so that total range is stride_len/2
        return (stride_len / 4.0) * tri_wave(phase)  # in [-stride/4, +stride/4]

    # Apply offsets only in x; keep y as rest; keep z=0 (as requested).
    # (This intentionally changes head-paw / tailroot-hindpaw edge lengths.)
    for paw, ph in ((lfp, gait_phase), (rhp, gait_phase),
                    (rfp, gait_phase + math.pi), (lhp, gait_phase + math.pi)):
        p0 = g.nodes[paw]
        nodes[paw] = np.array([p0[0] + paw_x_offset(ph), p0[1], 0.0], dtype=np.float64)

    # You may also want tail tip slight sway; keep length constraints out of scope here.
    return nodes, gait_phase


def pose_rearing_placeholder(
    g: MouseGraph,
    t_in_state: float,
    state_duration: float,
    rng: random.Random,
) -> Dict[str, np.ndarray]:
    """
    Simple rearing placeholder preserving head-ears-nose rigidity but not all edge lengths.
    (We can replace with strict kinematic version later if needed.)

    - pitch body cluster (head + tail root/tip) up and back around tail_root
    - lift/retract front paws a little
    """
    nodes = {k: v.copy() for k, v in g.nodes.items()}

    head = g.require("head")
    nose = g.require("nose_tip")
    le = g.require("left_ear_tip")
    re = g.require("right_ear_tip")
    tail_root = g.require("tail_root")
    tail_tip = g.require("tail_tip")
    lfp = g.require("left_front_paw")
    rfp = g.require("right_front_paw")

    u = 0.0 if state_duration <= 1e-9 else max(0.0, min(1.0, t_in_state / state_duration))
    h = math.sin(math.pi * u)  # 0..1..0

    # target pitch up around local y
    # modest: up to ~70 degrees
    pitch = math.radians(70.0) * h

    pivot = g.nodes[tail_root]
    Q = roty(pitch)

    # body cluster pivoted about tail root
    for key in (tail_tip, head, nose, le, re):
        v0 = g.nodes[key] - pivot
        nodes[key] = pivot + Q @ v0

    # keep ears-nose triangle rigid relative to head by re-applying rigid rotation around head
    head_pos = nodes[head].copy()
    # approximate head local rotation from the same Q (fine for placeholder)
    for key in (nose, le, re):
        v0 = g.nodes[key] - g.nodes[head]
        nodes[key] = head_pos + Q @ v0

    # front paws lift slightly (z) and retract (x)
    H = 0.6 * h
    Xr = 0.4 * h
    for paw in (lfp, rfp):
        p0 = g.nodes[paw]
        nodes[paw] = np.array([p0[0] - Xr, p0[1], max(0.0, p0[2]) + H], dtype=np.float64)

    return nodes


# ----------------------------
# Cameras and projection
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class Camera:
    name: str
    width: int
    height: int
    fx: float
    fy: float
    cx: float
    cy: float
    R: np.ndarray  # world->cam rotation (3x3)
    t: np.ndarray  # world->cam translation (3,)
    # for drawing (optional)
    pos_world: np.ndarray

    def project(self, Pw: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[float, float, bool]:
        """
        Pinhole projection. Returns (u,v,visible).
        Visible means in front of camera and within image bounds.
        """
        Pc = self.R @ Pw + self.t
        if Pc[2] <= 1e-9:
            return 0.0, 0.0, False
        u = self.fx * (Pc[0] / Pc[2]) + self.cx
        v = self.fy * (Pc[1] / Pc[2]) + self.cy
        visible = (0.0 <= u < self.width) and (0.0 <= v < self.height)
        return float(u), float(v), bool(visible)


def look_at(eye: np.ndarray, target: np.ndarray, up: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    """
    Returns (R, t) for world->camera.
    Camera looks along +Z in camera coords; we build a conventional pinhole:
      - z_cam = forward
      - x_cam = right
      - y_cam = down (image coordinates usually down)
    """
    fwd = target - eye
    fwd = fwd / (np.linalg.norm(fwd) + 1e-12)

    right = np.cross(fwd, up)
    right = right / (np.linalg.norm(right) + 1e-12)

    true_up = np.cross(right, fwd)
    true_up = true_up / (np.linalg.norm(true_up) + 1e-12)

    # Build rotation: rows are camera axes in world coords, but with y_cam pointing down.
    # camera coordinates:
    #   x = right
    #   y = -true_up (down)
    #   z = fwd
    Rcw = np.vstack([right, -true_up, fwd])  # cam axes in world coords (rows)
    R = Rcw  # world->cam rotation
    t = -R @ eye
    return R, t


def make_default_cameras(
    cage_w: float, cage_d: float, cage_h: float,
    image_w: int, image_h: int,
    fov_deg: float
) -> List[Camera]:
    # Center and corners for fitting
    C = np.array([cage_w/2, cage_d/2, cage_h/2], dtype=np.float64)
    corners = []
    for x in (0.0, cage_w):
        for y in (0.0, cage_d):
            for z in (0.0, cage_h):
                corners.append(np.array([x,y,z], dtype=np.float64))
    corners = np.array(corners)

    fov = math.radians(fov_deg)
    # choose focal from fov (horizontal)
    fx = (image_w/2) / math.tan(fov/2)
    fy = fx
    cx = image_w/2
    cy = image_h/2

    # radius of cage bounding sphere
    r = np.max(np.linalg.norm(corners - C, axis=1))
    # distance so that sphere fits (rough; conservative)
    dist = r / math.sin(fov/2) + 1e-6

    cams = []

    # Cam1 top-down
    eye1 = np.array([cage_w/2, cage_d/2, cage_h/2 + dist], dtype=np.float64)
    R1, t1 = look_at(eye1, C, np.array([0,1,0], dtype=np.float64))
    cams.append(Camera("cam1_top", image_w, image_h, fx, fy, cx, cy, R1, t1, eye1))

    # Cam2 front (looking from -y)
    eye2 = np.array([cage_w/2, cage_d/2 - dist, cage_h/2 + 0.25*cage_h], dtype=np.float64)
    R2, t2 = look_at(eye2, C, np.array([0,0,1], dtype=np.float64))
    cams.append(Camera("cam2_front", image_w, image_h, fx, fy, cx, cy, R2, t2, eye2))

    # Cam3 side (looking from -x)
    eye3 = np.array([cage_w/2 - dist, cage_d/2, cage_h/2 + 0.25*cage_h], dtype=np.float64)
    R3, t3 = look_at(eye3, C, np.array([0,0,1], dtype=np.float64))
    cams.append(Camera("cam3_side", image_w, image_h, fx, fy, cx, cy, R3, t3, eye3))

    return cams


# ----------------------------
# Rendering
# ----------------------------

def render_frame(
    cam: Camera,
    g: MouseGraph,
    world_nodes: Dict[str, np.ndarray],
    cage_w: float,
    cage_d: float,
    cage_h: float,
    draw_labels: bool = False
) -> np.ndarray:
    # Create blank image
    img = np.zeros((cam.height, cam.width, 3), dtype=np.uint8)

    # Draw cage wireframe (optional)
    cage_pts = []
    for x in (0.0, cage_w):
        for y in (0.0, cage_d):
            for z in (0.0, cage_h):
                cage_pts.append(np.array([x,y,z], dtype=np.float64))
    cage_pts = np.array(cage_pts)

    # edges between corners of a box
    corner_index = {(x,y,z): i for i,(x,y,z) in enumerate(
        [(x,y,z) for x in (0.0, cage_w) for y in (0.0, cage_d) for z in (0.0, cage_h)]
    )}
    def idx(x,y,z): return corner_index[(x,y,z)]
    box_edges = [
        (idx(0.0,0.0,0.0), idx(cage_w,0.0,0.0)),
        (idx(0.0,0.0,0.0), idx(0.0,cage_d,0.0)),
        (idx(cage_w,0.0,0.0), idx(cage_w,cage_d,0.0)),
        (idx(0.0,cage_d,0.0), idx(cage_w,cage_d,0.0)),
        (idx(0.0,0.0,cage_h), idx(cage_w,0.0,cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0,0.0,cage_h), idx(0.0,cage_d,cage_h)),
        (idx(cage_w,0.0,cage_h), idx(cage_w,cage_d,cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0,cage_d,cage_h), idx(cage_w,cage_d,cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0,0.0,0.0), idx(0.0,0.0,cage_h)),
        (idx(cage_w,0.0,0.0), idx(cage_w,0.0,cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0,cage_d,0.0), idx(0.0,cage_d,cage_h)),
        (idx(cage_w,cage_d,0.0), idx(cage_w,cage_d,cage_h)),
    ]
    cage_uv = []
    for p in cage_pts:
        u,v,vis = cam.project(p)
        cage_uv.append((u,v,vis))
    for a,b in box_edges:
        ua,va,va_vis = cage_uv[a]
        ub,vb,vb_vis = cage_uv[b]
        if va_vis and vb_vis and cv2 is not None:
            cv2.line(img, (int(ua),int(va)), (int(ub),int(vb)), (60,60,60), 1, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # Draw skeleton edges
    for a, b in g.edges:
        if a not in world_nodes or b not in world_nodes:
            continue
        ua, va, visa = cam.project(world_nodes[a])
        ub, vb, visb = cam.project(world_nodes[b])
        if not (visa and visb):
            continue
        if cv2 is not None:
            cv2.line(img, (int(ua), int(va)), (int(ub), int(vb)), (220, 220, 220), 2, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # Draw nodes
    for label, Pw in world_nodes.items():
        u, v, vis = cam.project(Pw)
        if not vis:
            continue
        if cv2 is not None:
            cv2.circle(img, (int(u), int(v)), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
            if draw_labels:
                cv2.putText(img, label, (int(u)+5, int(v)-5),
                            cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX, 0.4, (200,200,200), 1, cv2.LINE_AA)

    return img


# ----------------------------
# Main simulation
# ----------------------------

def simulate(args: argparse.Namespace) -> None:
    rng = random.Random(args.seed)

    g = load_mouse_graph(args.mouse_graph)

    # required nodes
    g.require("head")
    g.require("nose_tip")
    g.require("left_ear_tip")
    g.require("right_ear_tip")
    g.require("left_front_paw")
    g.require("right_front_paw")
    g.require("tail_root")
    g.require("left_hind_paw")
    g.require("right_hind_paw")
    g.require("tail_tip")

    # stride length = z_head / 3 (per your spec)
    z_head = float(g.nodes[_norm_label("head")][2])
    stride_len = z_head / 3.0 if z_head > 0 else args.stride_len_fallback

    os.makedirs(args.out_dir, exist_ok=True)

    # cameras
    cams = make_default_cameras(
        args.cage_width, args.cage_depth, args.cage_height,
        args.image_width, args.image_height,
        args.fov_deg
    )

    # writers
    video_writers = {}
    if args.write_video:
        if _VIDEO_BACKEND == "opencv":
            fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")  # type: ignore
            for cam in cams:
                path = os.path.join(args.out_dir, f"{cam.name}.mp4")
                video_writers[cam.name] = cv2.VideoWriter(path, fourcc, args.fps, (cam.width, cam.height))  # type: ignore
        elif _VIDEO_BACKEND == "imageio":
            for cam in cams:
                path = os.path.join(args.out_dir, f"{cam.name}.mp4")
                video_writers[cam.name] = imageio.get_writer(path, fps=args.fps)  # type: ignore
        else:
            print("Video backend not available; will skip video writing.")
            args.write_video = False

    # CSV outputs
    path_3d = os.path.join(args.out_dir, "coords_3d.csv")
    path_2d = {cam.name: os.path.join(args.out_dir, f"keypoints_{cam.name}.csv") for cam in cams}

    f3d = open(path_3d, "w", newline="", encoding="utf-8")
    w3d = csv.writer(f3d)
    w3d.writerow(["frame", "time", "behavior", "node", "x", "y", "z"])

    f2d = {}
    w2d = {}
    for cam in cams:
        f2d[cam.name] = open(path_2d[cam.name], "w", newline="", encoding="utf-8")
        w2d[cam.name] = csv.writer(f2d[cam.name])
        w2d[cam.name].writerow(["frame", "time", "behavior", "node", "u", "v", "visible"])

    # init track state (start near center)
    st = TrackState(
        x=args.cage_width * 0.5,
        y=args.cage_depth * 0.5,
        theta=rng.uniform(-math.pi, math.pi),
        v=rng.uniform(0.0, args.max_speed),
        omega=0.0
    )

    # behavior state
    beh = BehaviorState(
        behavior=0,
        t_in_state=0.0,
        state_duration=sample_duration(0, rng),
        gait_phase=rng.uniform(0.0, 2*math.pi),
    )

    dt = 1.0 / args.fps
    n_frames = int(round(args.duration * args.fps))

    for frame in range(n_frames):
        t = frame * dt

        # step behavior timer and maybe switch
        beh.t_in_state += dt
        if beh.t_in_state >= beh.state_duration:
            beh.behavior = next_behavior(beh.behavior, rng)
            beh.t_in_state = 0.0
            beh.state_duration = sample_duration(beh.behavior, rng)

        # step track (modulate by behavior)
        max_speed = args.max_speed * (args.rear_speed_scale if beh.behavior == 1 else 1.0)
        omega_noise = args.omega_noise * (args.rear_turn_noise_scale if beh.behavior == 1 else 1.0)

        st = step_track(
            st=st, dt=dt,
            cage_w=args.cage_width, cage_d=args.cage_depth,
            max_speed=max_speed,
            omega_max=args.omega_max,
            speed_noise=args.speed_noise,
            omega_noise=omega_noise,
            speed_damp=args.speed_damp,
            omega_damp=args.omega_damp,
            wall_repulse_gain=args.wall_repulse_gain,
            wall_repulse_dist=args.wall_repulse_dist,
            rng=rng
        )

        # local pose per behavior
        if beh.behavior == 0:
            local_nodes, beh.gait_phase = pose_running_option_a(
                g=g,
                dt=dt,
                v_body=st.v,
                gait_phase=beh.gait_phase,
                stride_len=stride_len,
                head_jitter_amp_deg=args.head_jitter_amp_deg,
                head_jitter_hz=args.head_jitter_hz,
                t_global=t,
                rng=rng
            )
        else:
            local_nodes = pose_rearing_placeholder(
                g=g,
                t_in_state=beh.t_in_state,
                state_duration=beh.state_duration,
                rng=rng
            )

        # transform to world
        R = rotz(st.theta)
        P = np.array([st.x, st.y, 0.0], dtype=np.float64)
        world_nodes = {k: (P + R @ v) for k, v in local_nodes.items()}

        # write 3D
        for node in g.node_order:
            Pw = world_nodes[node]
            w3d.writerow([frame, f"{t:.6f}", beh.behavior, node, f"{Pw[0]:.6f}", f"{Pw[1]:.6f}", f"{Pw[2]:.6f}"])

        # per-camera 2D + video
        for cam in cams:
            for node in g.node_order:
                u, v, vis = cam.project(world_nodes[node])
                w2d[cam.name].writerow([frame, f"{t:.6f}", beh.behavior, node, f"{u:.6f}", f"{v:.6f}", int(vis)])

            if args.write_video:
                img = render_frame(cam, g, world_nodes, args.cage_width, args.cage_depth, args.cage_height, draw_labels=args.draw_labels)
                if _VIDEO_BACKEND == "opencv":
                    video_writers[cam.name].write(img)  # type: ignore
                elif _VIDEO_BACKEND == "imageio":
                    video_writers[cam.name].append_data(img[..., ::-1])  # BGR->RGB-ish (frame is gray anyway)

    # close
    f3d.close()
    for cam in cams:
        f2d[cam.name].close()

    if args.write_video:
        if _VIDEO_BACKEND == "opencv":
            for vw in video_writers.values():
                vw.release()
        elif _VIDEO_BACKEND == "imageio":
            for vw in video_writers.values():
                vw.close()

    print(f"Done.\nOutputs in: {args.out_dir}")
    print(f"  3D coords: {path_3d}")
    for cam in cams:
        print(f"  2D keypoints: {path_2d[cam.name]}")
        if args.write_video:
            print(f"  Video: {os.path.join(args.out_dir, cam.name + '.mp4')}")


def build_argparser() -> argparse.ArgumentParser:
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Mouse 1.0 simulator (Option A trot).")
    p.add_argument("--mouse-graph", required=True, help="Path to mouse graph text file.")
    p.add_argument("--out-dir", default="out_mouse", help="Output directory.")

    # cage
    p.add_argument("--cage-width", type=float, default=40.0, help="Cage size in x.")
    p.add_argument("--cage-depth", type=float, default=30.0, help="Cage size in y.")
    p.add_argument("--cage-height", type=float, default=20.0, help="Cage height in z (for visualization).")

    # sim
    p.add_argument("--duration", type=float, default=20.0, help="Seconds to simulate.")
    p.add_argument("--fps", type=float, default=10.0, help="Frames per second (video + sampling).")
    p.add_argument("--seed", type=int, default=1, help="RNG seed.")

    # track dynamics
    p.add_argument("--max-speed", type=float, default=10.0, help="Max speed (units per second).")
    p.add_argument("--omega-max", type=float, default=2.2, help="Max yaw rate (rad/s).")
    p.add_argument("--speed-noise", type=float, default=6.0, help="Speed noise scale.")
    p.add_argument("--omega-noise", type=float, default=2.0, help="Yaw-rate noise scale.")
    p.add_argument("--speed-damp", type=float, default=1.5, help="Speed damping.")
    p.add_argument("--omega-damp", type=float, default=2.0, help="Yaw-rate damping.")
    p.add_argument("--wall-repulse-gain", type=float, default=2.0, help="Steering toward center near walls.")
    p.add_argument("--wall-repulse-dist", type=float, default=6.0, help="Wall proximity distance for repulsion.")

    # running gait
    p.add_argument("--stride-len-fallback", type=float, default=1.0, help="Used if head z<=0 in graph.")
    p.add_argument("--head-jitter-amp-deg", type=float, default=6.0, help="Head rigid-cluster jitter amplitude (deg).")
    p.add_argument("--head-jitter-hz", type=float, default=1.2, help="Head jitter frequency (Hz).")

    # rearing modulation
    p.add_argument("--rear-speed-scale", type=float, default=0.25, help="Speed multiplier during rearing.")
    p.add_argument("--rear-turn-noise-scale", type=float, default=1.2, help="Turn noise multiplier during rearing.")

    # camera/video
    p.add_argument("--image-width", type=int, default=960)
    p.add_argument("--image-height", type=int, default=720)
    p.add_argument("--fov-deg", type=float, default=60.0)
    p.add_argument("--write-video", action="store_true", help="Write mp4 videos (needs opencv or imageio).")
    p.add_argument("--draw-labels", action="store_true", help="Draw node labels into video frames.")
    return p


def main():
    args = build_argparser().parse_args()
    simulate(args)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### Expected `mouse.txt` format (minimal)
```txt
[NODES]
head 0 0 2.4
nose_tip 1.2 0 2.2
left_ear_tip 0.2 0.5 2.8
right_ear_tip 0.2 -0.5 2.8
left_front_paw 1.0 0.8 0
right_front_paw 1.0 -0.8 0
tail_root -1.0 0 1.2
left_hind_paw -1.4 0.6 0
right_hind_paw -1.4 -0.6 0
tail_tip -2.6 0 0.7

[EDGES]
head nose_tip
head left_ear_tip
head right_ear_tip
head left_front_paw
head right_front_paw
head tail_root
tail_root left_hind_paw
tail_root right_hind_paw
tail_root tail_tip
```

### Run example
```bash
python mouse_sim.py --mouse-graph mouse.txt --write-video --duration 30 --fps 10 --out-dir out
```

This will create in `out/`:
- `coords_3d.csv`
- `keypoints_cam1_top.csv`, `keypoints_cam2_front.csv`, `keypoints_cam3_side.csv`
- `cam1_top.mp4`, `cam2_front.mp4`, `cam3_side.mp4` (if a video backend is available)

If you want, next we can tighten the **rearing** definition to satisfy your “tail_root–head edge approximately vertical at peak” requirement *without* adding new joints.

User: Please add a protocol file recording times at which behavior class starts (switches) from 0 to 1.

Yes, tighten the rearing, please.

Assistant: ```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Mouse 1.0 — Option A (simple trot + tightened rearing + behavior protocol)

Changes vs previous version:
- Adds behavior_protocol.csv: records every switch 0 -> 1 (running -> rearing)
- Tightens rearing: rotates the body about tail_root so the tail_root->head axis is
  approximately vertical at peak of rearing (u=0.5), then returns.

Compromises remain (as agreed for Option A):
- During running, paws move on ground plane z=0 by local-x offsets (trot timing).
  This does not preserve head–paw / tailroot–hindpaw edge lengths.
"""

from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
import csv
import math
import os
import random
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np

# Optional video backend
_VIDEO_BACKEND = None
try:
    import cv2  # type: ignore
    _VIDEO_BACKEND = "opencv"
except Exception:
    cv2 = None  # type: ignore

if _VIDEO_BACKEND is None:
    try:
        import imageio  # type: ignore
        _VIDEO_BACKEND = "imageio"
    except Exception:
        imageio = None  # type: ignore


# ----------------------------
# File parsing (mouse graph)
# ----------------------------

def _norm_label(s: str) -> str:
    return s.strip().lower().replace(" ", "_")


@dataclass
class MouseGraph:
    nodes: Dict[str, np.ndarray]          # label -> (3,)
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]]          # (a,b)
    node_order: List[str]

    def require(self, label: str) -> str:
        key = _norm_label(label)
        if key not in self.nodes:
            raise ValueError(f"Mouse graph missing required node: {label}")
        return key


def load_mouse_graph(path: str) -> MouseGraph:
    """
    Minimal, forgiving format:

    [NODES]
    head  0.0 0.0 2.4
    nose_tip  1.2 0.0 2.2
    ...
    [EDGES]
    head nose_tip
    head left_ear_tip
    ...

    Lines starting with # are comments. Empty lines ignored.
    """
    if not os.path.exists(path):
        raise FileNotFoundError(path)

    mode = None
    nodes: Dict[str, np.ndarray] = {}
    edges: List[Tuple[str, str]] = []
    node_order: List[str] = []

    with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        for raw in f:
            line = raw.strip()
            if not line or line.startswith("#"):
                continue
            if line.upper() == "[NODES]":
                mode = "nodes"
                continue
            if line.upper() == "[EDGES]":
                mode = "edges"
                continue
            if mode == "nodes":
                parts = line.split()
                if len(parts) != 4:
                    raise ValueError(f"Bad node line: {line}")
                label = _norm_label(parts[0])
                x, y, z = map(float, parts[1:])
                if label in nodes:
                    raise ValueError(f"Duplicate node label: {label}")
                nodes[label] = np.array([x, y, z], dtype=np.float64)
                node_order.append(label)
            elif mode == "edges":
                parts = line.split()
                if len(parts) != 2:
                    raise ValueError(f"Bad edge line: {line}")
                a, b = _norm_label(parts[0]), _norm_label(parts[1])
                edges.append((a, b))
            else:
                raise ValueError(f"File must start with [NODES] section. Got: {line}")

    if not nodes:
        raise ValueError("No nodes loaded.")
    if not edges:
        raise ValueError("No edges loaded.")

    return MouseGraph(nodes=nodes, edges=edges, node_order=node_order)


# ----------------------------
# Math helpers
# ----------------------------

def rotz(theta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    c, s = math.cos(theta), math.sin(theta)
    return np.array([[c, -s, 0.0],
                     [s,  c, 0.0],
                     [0.0, 0.0, 1.0]], dtype=np.float64)

def roty(theta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    c, s = math.cos(theta), math.sin(theta)
    return np.array([[ c, 0.0, s],
                     [0.0, 1.0, 0.0],
                     [-s, 0.0, c]], dtype=np.float64)

def rotx(theta: float) -> np.ndarray:
    c, s = math.cos(theta), math.sin(theta)
    return np.array([[1.0, 0.0, 0.0],
                     [0.0,  c, -s],
                     [0.0,  s,  c]], dtype=np.float64)


# ----------------------------
# Random track model (smooth heading + speed)
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class TrackState:
    x: float
    y: float
    theta: float   # yaw heading
    v: float       # speed
    omega: float   # yaw rate


def step_track(
    st: TrackState,
    dt: float,
    cage_w: float,
    cage_d: float,
    max_speed: float,
    omega_max: float,
    speed_noise: float,
    omega_noise: float,
    speed_damp: float,
    omega_damp: float,
    wall_repulse_gain: float,
    wall_repulse_dist: float,
    rng: random.Random,
) -> TrackState:
    # OU-ish update
    st.v += (-speed_damp * st.v) * dt + speed_noise * math.sqrt(dt) * rng.gauss(0, 1)
    st.omega += (-omega_damp * st.omega) * dt + omega_noise * math.sqrt(dt) * rng.gauss(0, 1)

    st.v = max(0.0, min(max_speed, st.v))
    st.omega = max(-omega_max, min(omega_max, st.omega))

    # wall steering toward center near boundaries
    cx, cy = cage_w * 0.5, cage_d * 0.5
    to_c = math.atan2(cy - st.y, cx - st.x)

    def repulse(d: float) -> float:
        if d <= 1e-6:
            return 1.0
        if d >= wall_repulse_dist:
            return 0.0
        return (wall_repulse_dist - d) / wall_repulse_dist

    dL = st.x
    dR = cage_w - st.x
    dB = st.y
    dT = cage_d - st.y
    prox = max(repulse(dL), repulse(dR), repulse(dB), repulse(dT))

    def ang_diff(a: float, b: float) -> float:
        d = (a - b + math.pi) % (2 * math.pi) - math.pi
        return d

    steer = -wall_repulse_gain * prox * ang_diff(st.theta, to_c)

    st.theta += (st.omega + steer) * dt

    nx = st.x + st.v * dt * math.cos(st.theta)
    ny = st.y + st.v * dt * math.sin(st.theta)

    # reflect at hard boundaries
    if nx < 0.0 or nx > cage_w:
        st.theta = math.pi - st.theta
        nx = min(max(nx, 0.0), cage_w)
    if ny < 0.0 or ny > cage_d:
        st.theta = -st.theta
        ny = min(max(ny, 0.0), cage_d)

    st.x, st.y = nx, ny
    return st


# ----------------------------
# Behaviors
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class BehaviorState:
    behavior: int
    t_in_state: float
    state_duration: float
    # running gait
    gait_phase: float  # radians
    # rearing individualized params (sampled at behavior entry)
    rear_pitch_scale: float
    rear_paw_lift: float
    rear_paw_retract: float


def sample_duration(behavior: int, rng: random.Random) -> float:
    if behavior == 0:  # running
        return rng.uniform(2.0, 6.0)
    else:              # rearing
        return rng.uniform(0.6, 1.6)

def next_behavior(current: int, rng: random.Random) -> int:
    if current == 0:
        return 1 if rng.random() < 0.25 else 0
    else:
        return 0


def sample_rearing_params(rng: random.Random) -> Tuple[float, float, float]:
    """
    Small individuality per rearing bout.
    Returns: (pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract)
    """
    pitch_scale = 1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.08, 0.08)  # ±8%
    paw_lift = 0.7 * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
    paw_retract = 0.5 * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
    return pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract


def pose_running_option_a(
    g: MouseGraph,
    dt: float,
    v_body: float,
    gait_phase: float,
    stride_len: float,
    head_jitter_amp_deg: float,
    head_jitter_hz: float,
    t_global: float,
) -> Tuple[Dict[str, np.ndarray], float]:
    """
    Running pose:
    - head-ears-nose cluster stays rigid via small rotations around head
    - paws remain on z=0 and move in local x only, with diagonal trot timing.
    """
    nodes = {k: v.copy() for k, v in g.nodes.items()}

    head = g.require("head")
    nose = g.require("nose_tip")
    le = g.require("left_ear_tip")
    re = g.require("right_ear_tip")
    lfp = g.require("left_front_paw")
    rfp = g.require("right_front_paw")
    lhp = g.require("left_hind_paw")
    rhp = g.require("right_hind_paw")

    # --- rigid head cluster jitter (keeps ears-nose triangle rigid) ---
    A = math.radians(head_jitter_amp_deg)
    w = 2 * math.pi * head_jitter_hz
    pitch = A * math.sin(w * t_global + 0.3)
    roll  = A * 0.7 * math.sin(w * t_global + 1.1)
    yaw   = A * 0.5 * math.sin(w * t_global + 2.0)
    Q = rotz(yaw) @ rotx(roll) @ roty(pitch)

    head_pos = nodes[head].copy()
    for key in (nose, le, re):
        v0 = g.nodes[key] - g.nodes[head]
        nodes[key] = head_pos + Q @ v0

    # --- gait phase advance tied to speed ---
    if stride_len <= 1e-9 or v_body <= 1e-9:
        dphi = 0.0
    else:
        dphi = 2 * math.pi * (v_body / stride_len) * dt
    gait_phase = (gait_phase + dphi) % (2 * math.pi)

    # triangle wave in [-1,1]
    def tri_wave(phase: float) -> float:
        u = (phase % (2 * math.pi)) / (2 * math.pi)
        if u < 0.5:
            return 1.0 - 4.0 * u   # 1 -> -1
        else:
            return -3.0 + 4.0 * u  # -1 -> 1

    # Range in x is about stride_len/2 total (±stride/4)
    def paw_x_offset(phase: float) -> float:
        return (stride_len / 4.0) * tri_wave(phase)

    # diagonal pairing:
    # Pair A: LFP + RHP use phase φ
    # Pair B: RFP + LHP use phase φ+π
    for paw, ph in (
        (lfp, gait_phase),
        (rhp, gait_phase),
        (rfp, gait_phase + math.pi),
        (lhp, gait_phase + math.pi),
    ):
        p0 = g.nodes[paw]
        nodes[paw] = np.array([p0[0] + paw_x_offset(ph), p0[1], 0.0], dtype=np.float64)

    return nodes, gait_phase


def pose_rearing_tight(
    g: MouseGraph,
    t_in_state: float,
    state_duration: float,
    rear_pitch_scale: float,
    rear_paw_lift: float,
    rear_paw_retract: float,
) -> Dict[str, np.ndarray]:
    """
    Tightened rearing (still simple):

    Goal: at peak (u=0.5) rotate the body around tail_root such that
    the vector (tail_root -> head) is ~vertical (parallel to +z),
    then return to rest by u=1.

    Time envelope: h(u) = sin(pi*u), giving 0..1..0.
    """
    nodes = {k: v.copy() for k, v in g.nodes.items()}

    head = g.require("head")
    nose = g.require("nose_tip")
    le = g.require("left_ear_tip")
    re = g.require("right_ear_tip")
    tail_root = g.require("tail_root")
    tail_tip = g.require("tail_tip")
    lfp = g.require("left_front_paw")
    rfp = g.require("right_front_paw")
    lhp = g.require("left_hind_paw")
    rhp = g.require("right_hind_paw")

    u = 0.0 if state_duration <= 1e-9 else max(0.0, min(1.0, t_in_state / state_duration))
    h = math.sin(math.pi * u)  # 0..1..0

    # Compute required pitch (around local y) to make (tail_root->head) vertical at peak.
    a0 = g.nodes[head] - g.nodes[tail_root]
    # assume near symmetry => y component small; use x-z plane
    alpha0 = math.atan2(float(a0[2]), float(a0[0]))  # angle from +x toward +z
    alpha_target = math.pi / 2.0
    delta = alpha_target - alpha0
    pitch = (delta * rear_pitch_scale) * h

    pivot = g.nodes[tail_root]
    Q = roty(pitch)

    # Rotate a body cluster about tail_root; this makes tail_root->head vertical at peak.
    # Include head cluster + tail tip. (tail_root stays fixed).
    body_cluster = (head, nose, le, re, tail_tip)
    for key in body_cluster:
        v0 = g.nodes[key] - pivot
        nodes[key] = pivot + Q @ v0

    # Hind paws stay on ground (cheap): keep them at rest on z=0.
    # (If rest z isn't 0, we force z=0 for this simulation.)
    for key in (lhp, rhp):
        p0 = g.nodes[key]
        nodes[key] = np.array([p0[0], p0[1], 0.0], dtype=np.float64)

    # Front paws lift and retract during rearing; keep y fixed; z rises then falls
    for paw in (lfp, rfp):
        p0 = g.nodes[paw]
        nodes[paw] = np.array([p0[0] - rear_paw_retract * h, p0[1], rear_paw_lift * h], dtype=np.float64)

    return nodes


# ----------------------------
# Cameras and projection
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class Camera:
    name: str
    width: int
    height: int
    fx: float
    fy: float
    cx: float
    cy: float
    R: np.ndarray  # world->cam rotation (3x3)
    t: np.ndarray  # world->cam translation (3,)
    pos_world: np.ndarray

    def project(self, Pw: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[float, float, bool]:
        Pc = self.R @ Pw + self.t
        if Pc[2] <= 1e-9:
            return 0.0, 0.0, False
        u = self.fx * (Pc[0] / Pc[2]) + self.cx
        v = self.fy * (Pc[1] / Pc[2]) + self.cy
        visible = (0.0 <= u < self.width) and (0.0 <= v < self.height)
        return float(u), float(v), bool(visible)


def look_at(eye: np.ndarray, target: np.ndarray, up: np.ndarray) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    """
    world->camera where cam axes are:
      x: right, y: down, z: forward
    """
    fwd = target - eye
    fwd = fwd / (np.linalg.norm(fwd) + 1e-12)

    right = np.cross(fwd, up)
    right = right / (np.linalg.norm(right) + 1e-12)

    true_up = np.cross(right, fwd)
    true_up = true_up / (np.linalg.norm(true_up) + 1e-12)

    Rcw = np.vstack([right, -true_up, fwd])
    R = Rcw
    t = -R @ eye
    return R, t


def make_default_cameras(
    cage_w: float, cage_d: float, cage_h: float,
    image_w: int, image_h: int,
    fov_deg: float
) -> List[Camera]:
    C = np.array([cage_w/2, cage_d/2, cage_h/2], dtype=np.float64)
    corners = []
    for x in (0.0, cage_w):
        for y in (0.0, cage_d):
            for z in (0.0, cage_h):
                corners.append(np.array([x, y, z], dtype=np.float64))
    corners = np.array(corners)

    fov = math.radians(fov_deg)
    fx = (image_w / 2) / math.tan(fov / 2)
    fy = fx
    cx = image_w / 2
    cy = image_h / 2

    r = np.max(np.linalg.norm(corners - C, axis=1))
    dist = r / math.sin(fov / 2) + 1e-6

    cams = []
    # top
    eye1 = np.array([cage_w/2, cage_d/2, cage_h/2 + dist], dtype=np.float64)
    R1, t1 = look_at(eye1, C, np.array([0, 1, 0], dtype=np.float64))
    cams.append(Camera("cam1_top", image_w, image_h, fx, fy, cx, cy, R1, t1, eye1))
    # front (-y)
    eye2 = np.array([cage_w/2, cage_d/2 - dist, cage_h/2 + 0.25*cage_h], dtype=np.float64)
    R2, t2 = look_at(eye2, C, np.array([0, 0, 1], dtype=np.float64))
    cams.append(Camera("cam2_front", image_w, image_h, fx, fy, cx, cy, R2, t2, eye2))
    # side (-x)
    eye3 = np.array([cage_w/2 - dist, cage_d/2, cage_h/2 + 0.25*cage_h], dtype=np.float64)
    R3, t3 = look_at(eye3, C, np.array([0, 0, 1], dtype=np.float64))
    cams.append(Camera("cam3_side", image_w, image_h, fx, fy, cx, cy, R3, t3, eye3))
    return cams


# ----------------------------
# Rendering
# ----------------------------

def render_frame(
    cam: Camera,
    g: MouseGraph,
    world_nodes: Dict[str, np.ndarray],
    cage_w: float,
    cage_d: float,
    cage_h: float,
    draw_labels: bool = False
) -> np.ndarray:
    img = np.zeros((cam.height, cam.width, 3), dtype=np.uint8)

    if cv2 is None:
        return img

    # cage corners
    cage_pts = []
    for x in (0.0, cage_w):
        for y in (0.0, cage_d):
            for z in (0.0, cage_h):
                cage_pts.append(np.array([x, y, z], dtype=np.float64))
    cage_pts = np.array(cage_pts)

    corner_index = {(x, y, z): i for i, (x, y, z) in enumerate(
        [(x, y, z) for x in (0.0, cage_w) for y in (0.0, cage_d) for z in (0.0, cage_h)]
    )}
    def idx(x, y, z): return corner_index[(x, y, z)]
    box_edges = [
        (idx(0.0, 0.0, 0.0), idx(cage_w, 0.0, 0.0)),
        (idx(0.0, 0.0, 0.0), idx(0.0, cage_d, 0.0)),
        (idx(cage_w, 0.0, 0.0), idx(cage_w, cage_d, 0.0)),
        (idx(0.0, cage_d, 0.0), idx(cage_w, cage_d, 0.0)),
        (idx(0.0, 0.0, cage_h), idx(cage_w, 0.0, cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0, 0.0, cage_h), idx(0.0, cage_d, cage_h)),
        (idx(cage_w, 0.0, cage_h), idx(cage_w, cage_d, cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0, cage_d, cage_h), idx(cage_w, cage_d, cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0, 0.0, 0.0), idx(0.0, 0.0, cage_h)),
        (idx(cage_w, 0.0, 0.0), idx(cage_w, 0.0, cage_h)),
        (idx(0.0, cage_d, 0.0), idx(0.0, cage_d, cage_h)),
        (idx(cage_w, cage_d, 0.0), idx(cage_w, cage_d, cage_h)),
    ]
    cage_uv = []
    for p in cage_pts:
        u, v, vis = cam.project(p)
        cage_uv.append((u, v, vis))
    for a, b in box_edges:
        ua, va, va_vis = cage_uv[a]
        ub, vb, vb_vis = cage_uv[b]
        if va_vis and vb_vis:
            cv2.line(img, (int(ua), int(va)), (int(ub), int(vb)), (60, 60, 60), 1, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # skeleton edges
    for a, b in g.edges:
        if a not in world_nodes or b not in world_nodes:
            continue
        ua, va, visa = cam.project(world_nodes[a])
        ub, vb, visb = cam.project(world_nodes[b])
        if visa and visb:
            cv2.line(img, (int(ua), int(va)), (int(ub), int(vb)), (220, 220, 220), 2, cv2.LINE_AA)

    # nodes
    for label, Pw in world_nodes.items():
        u, v, vis = cam.project(Pw)
        if not vis:
            continue
        cv2.circle(img, (int(u), int(v)), 4, (255, 255, 255), -1, cv2.LINE_AA)
        if draw_labels:
            cv2.putText(img, label, (int(u) + 5, int(v) - 5),
                        cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX, 0.4, (200, 200, 200), 1, cv2.LINE_AA)

    return img


# ----------------------------
# Main simulation
# ----------------------------

def simulate(args: argparse.Namespace) -> None:
    rng = random.Random(args.seed)

    g = load_mouse_graph(args.mouse_graph)

    # required nodes
    for req in [
        "head", "nose_tip", "left_ear_tip", "right_ear_tip",
        "left_front_paw", "right_front_paw",
        "tail_root", "left_hind_paw", "right_hind_paw", "tail_tip"
    ]:
        g.require(req)

    # stride length = z_head / 3
    z_head = float(g.nodes[_norm_label("head")][2])
    stride_len = z_head / 3.0 if z_head > 0 else args.stride_len_fallback

    os.makedirs(args.out_dir, exist_ok=True)

    # cameras
    cams = make_default_cameras(
        args.cage_width, args.cage_depth, args.cage_height,
        args.image_width, args.image_height,
        args.fov_deg
    )

    # writers (video)
    video_writers = {}
    if args.write_video:
        if _VIDEO_BACKEND == "opencv":
            fourcc = cv2.VideoWriter_fourcc(*"mp4v")  # type: ignore
            for cam in cams:
                path = os.path.join(args.out_dir, f"{cam.name}.mp4")
                video_writers[cam.name] = cv2.VideoWriter(path, fourcc, args.fps, (cam.width, cam.height))  # type: ignore
        elif _VIDEO_BACKEND == "imageio":
            for cam in cams:
                path = os.path.join(args.out_dir, f"{cam.name}.mp4")
                video_writers[cam.name] = imageio.get_writer(path, fps=args.fps)  # type: ignore
        else:
            print("Video backend not available; will skip video writing.")
            args.write_video = False

    # CSV outputs
    path_3d = os.path.join(args.out_dir, "coords_3d.csv")
    path_protocol = os.path.join(args.out_dir, "behavior_protocol.csv")
    path_2d = {cam.name: os.path.join(args.out_dir, f"keypoints_{cam.name}.csv") for cam in cams}

    f3d = open(path_3d, "w", newline="", encoding="utf-8")
    w3d = csv.writer(f3d)
    w3d.writerow(["frame", "time", "behavior", "node", "x", "y", "z"])

    fproto = open(path_protocol, "w", newline="", encoding="utf-8")
    wproto = csv.writer(fproto)
    # record only 0 -> 1 starts, per your request
    wproto.writerow(["frame", "time", "from_behavior", "to_behavior", "rearing_duration",
                     "rear_pitch_scale", "rear_paw_lift", "rear_paw_retract"])

    f2d = {}
    w2d = {}
    for cam in cams:
        f2d[cam.name] = open(path_2d[cam.name], "w", newline="", encoding="utf-8")
        w2d[cam.name] = csv.writer(f2d[cam.name])
        w2d[cam.name].writerow(["frame", "time", "behavior", "node", "u", "v", "visible"])

    # init track state
    st = TrackState(
        x=args.cage_width * 0.5,
        y=args.cage_depth * 0.5,
        theta=rng.uniform(-math.pi, math.pi),
        v=rng.uniform(0.0, args.max_speed),
        omega=0.0
    )

    # init behavior state
    pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(rng)
    beh = BehaviorState(
        behavior=0,
        t_in_state=0.0,
        state_duration=sample_duration(0, rng),
        gait_phase=rng.uniform(0.0, 2 * math.pi),
        rear_pitch_scale=pitch_scale,
        rear_paw_lift=paw_lift,
        rear_paw_retract=paw_retract,
    )

    dt = 1.0 / args.fps
    n_frames = int(round(args.duration * args.fps))

    for frame in range(n_frames):
        t = frame * dt

        # step behavior timer and maybe switch
        beh.t_in_state += dt
        if beh.t_in_state >= beh.state_duration:
            prev = beh.behavior
            newb = next_behavior(beh.behavior, rng)
            beh.behavior = newb
            beh.t_in_state = 0.0
            beh.state_duration = sample_duration(beh.behavior, rng)

            # if entering rearing, sample parameters and write protocol entry (only 0->1)
            if prev == 0 and newb == 1:
                beh.rear_pitch_scale, beh.rear_paw_lift, beh.rear_paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(rng)
                wproto.writerow([
                    frame, f"{t:.6f}", prev, newb, f"{beh.state_duration:.6f}",
                    f"{beh.rear_pitch_scale:.6f}", f"{beh.rear_paw_lift:.6f}", f"{beh.rear_paw_retract:.6f}"
                ])

        # step track (modulate by behavior)
        max_speed = args.max_speed * (args.rear_speed_scale if beh.behavior == 1 else 1.0)
        omega_noise = args.omega_noise * (args.rear_turn_noise_scale if beh.behavior == 1 else 1.0)

        st = step_track(
            st=st, dt=dt,
            cage_w=args.cage_width, cage_d=args.cage_depth,
            max_speed=max_speed,
            omega_max=args.omega_max,
            speed_noise=args.speed_noise,
            omega_noise=omega_noise,
            speed_damp=args.speed_damp,
            omega_damp=args.omega_damp,
            wall_repulse_gain=args.wall_repulse_gain,
            wall_repulse_dist=args.wall_repulse_dist,
            rng=rng
        )

        # local pose
        if beh.behavior == 0:
            local_nodes, beh.gait_phase = pose_running_option_a(
                g=g,
                dt=dt,
                v_body=st.v,
                gait_phase=beh.gait_phase,
                stride_len=stride_len,
                head_jitter_amp_deg=args.head_jitter_amp_deg,
                head_jitter_hz=args.head_jitter_hz,
                t_global=t,
            )
        else:
            local_nodes = pose_rearing_tight(
                g=g,
                t_in_state=beh.t_in_state,
                state_duration=beh.state_duration,
                rear_pitch_scale=beh.rear_pitch_scale,
                rear_paw_lift=beh.rear_paw_lift,
                rear_paw_retract=beh.rear_paw_retract,
            )

        # transform to world
        R = rotz(st.theta)
        P = np.array([st.x, st.y, 0.0], dtype=np.float64)
        world_nodes = {k: (P + R @ v) for k, v in local_nodes.items()}

        # write 3D
        for node in g.node_order:
            Pw = world_nodes[node]
            w3d.writerow([frame, f"{t:.6f}", beh.behavior, node,
                          f"{Pw[0]:.6f}", f"{Pw[1]:.6f}", f"{Pw[2]:.6f}"])

        # per-camera 2D + video
        for cam in cams:
            for node in g.node_order:
                u, v, vis = cam.project(world_nodes[node])
                w2d[cam.name].writerow([frame, f"{t:.6f}", beh.behavior, node,
                                        f"{u:.6f}", f"{v:.6f}", int(vis)])

            if args.write_video:
                img = render_frame(cam, g, world_nodes,
                                   args.cage_width, args.cage_depth, args.cage_height,
                                   draw_labels=args.draw_labels)
                if _VIDEO_BACKEND == "opencv":
                    video_writers[cam.name].write(img)  # type: ignore
                elif _VIDEO_BACKEND == "imageio":
                    # imageio expects RGB; our render uses cv2 colors (BGR-ish), but mostly grayscale.
                    video_writers[cam.name].append_data(img[..., ::-1])  # type: ignore

    # close
    f3d.close()
    fproto.close()
    for cam in cams:
        f2d[cam.name].close()

    if args.write_video:
        if _VIDEO_BACKEND == "opencv":
            for vw in video_writers.values():
                vw.release()
        elif _VIDEO_BACKEND == "imageio":
            for vw in video_writers.values():
                vw.close()

    print(f"Done.\nOutputs in: {args.out_dir}")
    print(f"  3D coords: {path_3d}")
    print(f"  Behavior protocol (0->1): {path_protocol}")
    for cam in cams:
        print(f"  2D keypoints: {path_2d[cam.name]}")
        if args.write_video:
            print(f"  Video: {os.path.join(args.out_dir, cam.name + '.mp4')}")


def build_argparser() -> argparse.ArgumentParser:
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser(description="Mouse 1.0 simulator (Option A trot).")
    p.add_argument("--mouse-graph", required=True, help="Path to mouse graph text file.")
    p.add_argument("--out-dir", default="out_mouse", help="Output directory.")

    # cage
    p.add_argument("--cage-width", type=float, default=40.0, help="Cage size in x.")
    p.add_argument("--cage-depth", type=float, default=30.0, help="Cage size in y.")
    p.add_argument("--cage-height", type=float, default=20.0, help="Cage height in z (for visualization).")

    # sim
    p.add_argument("--duration", type=float, default=20.0, help="Seconds to simulate.")
    p.add_argument("--fps", type=float, default=10.0, help="Frames per second (video + sampling).")
    p.add_argument("--seed", type=int, default=1, help="RNG seed.")

    # track dynamics
    p.add_argument("--max-speed", type=float, default=10.0, help="Max speed (units per second).")
    p.add_argument("--omega-max", type=float, default=2.2, help="Max yaw rate (rad/s).")
    p.add_argument("--speed-noise", type=float, default=6.0, help="Speed noise scale.")
    p.add_argument("--omega-noise", type=float, default=2.0, help="Yaw-rate noise scale.")
    p.add_argument("--speed-damp", type=float, default=1.5, help="Speed damping.")
    p.add_argument("--omega-damp", type=float, default=2.0, help="Yaw-rate damping.")
    p.add_argument("--wall-repulse-gain", type=float, default=2.0, help="Steering toward center near walls.")
    p.add_argument("--wall-repulse-dist", type=float, default=6.0, help="Wall proximity distance for repulsion.")

    # running gait
    p.add_argument("--stride-len-fallback", type=float, default=1.0, help="Used if head z<=0 in graph.")
    p.add_argument("--head-jitter-amp-deg", type=float, default=6.0, help="Head rigid-cluster jitter amplitude (deg).")
    p.add_argument("--head-jitter-hz", type=float, default=1.2, help="Head jitter frequency (Hz).")

    # rearing modulation
    p.add_argument("--rear-speed-scale", type=float, default=0.25, help="Speed multiplier during rearing.")
    p.add_argument("--rear-turn-noise-scale", type=float, default=1.2, help="Turn noise multiplier during rearing.")

    # camera/video
    p.add_argument("--image-width", type=int, default=960)
    p.add_argument("--image-height", type=int, default=720)
    p.add_argument("--fov-deg", type=float, default=60.0)
    p.add_argument("--write-video", action="store_true", help="Write mp4 videos (needs opencv or imageio).")
    p.add_argument("--draw-labels", action="store_true", help="Draw node labels into video frames.")
    return p


def main():
    args = build_argparser().parse_args()
    simulate(args)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

### What you get now
- `behavior_protocol.csv` contains **only** `0 -> 1` transitions (start of rearing), with the sampled rearing duration and the per-bout individuality parameters.
- Rearing now explicitly rotates the body around `tail_root` so that at the peak (midpoint of the rearing interval) the **tail_root→head vector is as close to vertical as a pure y-axis pitch can make it** (exact when the rest pose is symmetric with `y≈0` along that axis).

If you want the rearing to *also* keep hind paws fixed on the ground in world space (even while the body pitches), we can do that next—but it will require either accepting more geometric inconsistency (like we already do for running) or adding intermediate joints (Option B).

User: I would like to run the program in a conda environment. Please give me a environment.yml to install it.

Assistant: Here’s a solid `environment.yml` for a Conda env that will run the simulator and (optionally) write MP4 videos. It prefers `opencv` for video output; if that’s not available on your platform, you can still run everything else (CSV outputs) and/or use `imageio-ffmpeg`.

```yaml
name: mouse-sim
channels:
  - conda-forge
dependencies:
  - python=3.11
  - numpy
  - pip

  # Video + drawing (recommended)
  - opencv

  # Optional fallback video writer
  - imageio
  - imageio-ffmpeg

  # Nice-to-have utilities
  - tqdm

  # If you want to run as a module / lint later (optional)
  # - ipython
  # - black
  # - ruff
```

### Use it
```bash
conda env create -f environment.yml
conda activate mouse-sim
python mouse_sim.py --mouse-graph mouse.txt --write-video --duration 30 --fps 10 --out-dir out
```

Notes:
- If `opencv` is installed, the script will use it to render and write MP4s.
- If `opencv` isn’t available for some reason, the env still includes `imageio` + `imageio-ffmpeg` as a fallback (the script will choose what it finds).

User: On first attempt the program generated the videos. It looks plausible, how the mouse moves. However, I did not recognize any rearing. And the behaviour_protocol.csv does not seem to contain anything but a headline.

Assistant: What you’re seeing is consistent with how the current state machine is written, not (necessarily) a projection/video bug:

- A **rearing bout only happens on a transition where `next_behavior(0)` returns `1`**.
- In the code I gave you, that happens with probability **0.25** each time a running segment ends.
- Running segments last **2–6 s**. In a **20 s** simulation you’ll typically get only a handful of “decision points”, so it’s entirely possible to get **zero** rears (and then `behavior_protocol.csv` will contain only the header).

### Quick sanity check (no code changes)
Try one of these and you should almost certainly see rearing and protocol entries:

```bash

```

or just change the seed a couple times.

## Make rearing reliably appear (recommended fix)
Add two CLI parameters:

- `--p-rear` : probability to start rearing when a running bout ends
- `--force-rear-after` : maximum time allowed without a rear; if exceeded, force the next decision to be rearing

### 1) Replace `next_behavior` with this
```python
def next_behavior(current: int, rng: random.Random, p_rear: float, force_rear: bool) -> int:
    if current == 0:
        if force_rear:
            return 1
        return 1 if rng.random() < p_rear else 0
    else:
        return 0
```

### 2) Add arguments to `build_argparser()`
```python
p.add_argument("--p-rear", type=float, default=0.35,
               help="Probability to switch from running (0) to rearing (1) when a running bout ends.")
p.add_argument("--force-rear-after", type=float, default=12.0,
               help="Force a rearing bout if no rearing happened for this many seconds (0 disables).")
```

### 3) In `simulate()`, track time since last rearing
Initialize near the behavior state creation:
```python
time_since_last_rear = 0.0
```

Update each frame *before* the switch decision:
```python
if beh.behavior == 1:
    time_since_last_rear = 0.0
else:
    time_since_last_rear += dt
```

Then, when the bout ends, compute `force_rear` and call the new `next_behavior`:
```python
if beh.t_in_state >= beh.state_duration:
    prev = beh.behavior

    force_rear = (args.force_rear_after > 0.0) and (time_since_last_rear >= args.force_rear_after)
    newb = next_behavior(prev, rng, args.p_rear, force_rear)

    beh.behavior = newb
    beh.t_in_state = 0.0
    beh.state_duration = sample_duration(newb, rng)

    if prev == 0 and newb == 1:
        beh.rear_pitch_scale, beh.rear_paw_lift, beh.rear_paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(rng)
        wproto.writerow([... same as before ...])
        time_since_last_rear = 0.0
```

### 4) Run with explicit rearing probability
```bash
python mouse_sim.py --mouse-graph mouse.txt --write-video --duration 30 --fps 10 \
  --p-rear 0.5 --force-rear-after 8 --out-dir out3
```

This will:
- **guarantee** you eventually get rearing even with “unlucky” seeds,
- and your `behavior_protocol.csv` will always get entries once rearing occurs.

Your current rearing *is* “tight” in the sense that at peak it tries to pitch the tail_root→head axis to vertical (via a y-axis pitch in local space). But you didn’t see it because the state never triggered.

- the sampled `rear_pitch_scale` range (increase from ±8% to e.g. ±15%)

Assistant: You’re right: that’s a sign error in the rearing pitch (given the `roty()` matrix I coded).

### What happened (in one sentence)
With my `roty(θ)`, **positive** `θ` rotates a forward (+x) vector **toward −z**, i.e. it *lowers* the head direction; to raise it toward +z you need the **negative** angle.

---

## Fix: compute the pitch that makes tail_root→head vertical, then apply it with the correct sign

Replace the pitch computation block inside `pose_rearing_tight()` with this (drop the old `alpha0/delta` math):

```python
    # Compute pitch_peak so that after rotation the (tail_root->head) vector has x'≈0, z'>0.
    a0 = g.nodes[head] - g.nodes[tail_root]
    ax = float(a0[0])
    az = float(a0[2])

    # Solve x' = cos(p)*ax + sin(p)*az = 0  =>  p = atan2(-ax, az)
    pitch_peak = math.atan2(-ax, az)  # NOTE the minus sign

    # time envelope 0..1..0
    u = 0.0 if state_duration <= 1e-9 else max(0.0, min(1.0, t_in_state / state_duration))
    h = math.sin(math.pi * u)

    pitch = (pitch_peak * rear_pitch_scale) * h
    Q = roty(pitch)
```

That’s it. With this, at peak rearing (`u≈0.5`, `h=1`) the `tail_root→head` axis is driven to vertical (in the x–z plane), instead of being flattened.

### Why this is robust
It directly solves the condition `x' = 0` under your exact `roty()` definition, so it’s not sensitive to quadrant issues like `atan2(z,x)` vs `pi/2 - ...`.

```python
        a1 = Q @ a0
        print("rear check:", "x'=", float(a1[0]), "z'=", float(a1[2]))
```

You should see `x'` close to 0 and `z'` positive at peak.

```python
    # time envelope 0..1..0
    u = 0.0 if state_duration <= 1e-9 else max(0.0, min(1.0, t_in_state / state_duration))
    h = math.sin(math.pi * u)  # 0..1..0

    # Compute pitch_peak so that after rotation the (tail_root->head) vector has x'≈0, z'>0.
    a0 = g.nodes[head] - g.nodes[tail_root]
    ax = float(a0[0])
    az = float(a0[2])

    # With roty() as defined: x' = cos(p)*ax + sin(p)*az
```

User: The units of cage and mouse.txt seem to be in cm. I would rather work in mm. Is there anything else I would need to change to let this take effect and not destroy/deform anything?

Assistant: You can switch to **mm** without breaking anything, as long as you apply **one consistent scale** to *all length-like quantities* (mouse model, cage dimensions, and any parameters measured in length or length/time). The simulator is unitless; it only cares about *ratios*.

### The one rule
If you currently treat numbers as **cm** and you want **mm**, use a scale factor:

- `S = 10` (because 1 cm = 10 mm)

Then:

- every **position / length** → multiply by `S`
- every **speed** (length/sec) → multiply by `S`
- every **angular** quantity (rad, deg), **fps**, probabilities → **unchanged**

---

## What you need to change (checklist)

### 1) `mouse.txt` node coordinates
Multiply every coordinate by 10.

Example: `head 0 0 2.4` (cm) → `head 0 0 24.0` (mm)

### 2) Cage dimensions (CLI args)
Multiply these by 10:

- `--cage-width`
- `--cage-depth`
- `--cage-height`

So e.g. `40 × 30 × 20` (cm) → `400 × 300 × 200` (mm)

### 3) Motion parameters that are lengths or depend on lengths
Multiply these by 10:

- `--max-speed`  (now mm/s)
- `--wall-repulse-dist`
- `--stride-len-fallback` (only used if head.z ≤ 0)

**No other track parameters need scaling**:
- `--omega-max`, `--omega-noise`, `--omega-damp` are angular; keep same.
- `--speed-noise` *is in speed units*, so if you care about identical “feel”, scale it by 10 too. (Otherwise the motion will look “less noisy” relative to the bigger mm scale.)

So: also multiply
- `--speed-noise` by 10

### 4) Rearing constants inside the code (important)
Right now, rearing uses **hard-coded** values like `paw_lift = 0.7` and `paw_retract = 0.5` in *model units*. If you change units to mm but don’t adjust these, the paws will barely move.

You have two clean options:

**Option A (quick): scale them by 10 in the code**
In `sample_rearing_params()`:
```python
paw_lift = 7.0 * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
paw_retract = 5.0 * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
```

**Option B (better): make them relative to mouse size (unit-invariant)**
Pass `z_head` into `sample_rearing_params(z_head, rng)` and do:
```python
paw_lift = 0.30 * z_head * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
paw_retract = 0.20 * z_head * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
```
This way, switching cm↔mm never requires touching these again.

Nothing special needed:
- FOV is dimensionless
- pixel sizes are pixels

## Patch: make rearing paw lift/retract scale with `z_head`

### 1) Change `sample_rearing_params` signature + implementation

Replace:

```python
def sample_rearing_params(rng: random.Random) -> Tuple[float, float, float]:
    pitch_scale = 1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.08, 0.08)
    paw_lift = 0.7 * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
    paw_retract = 0.5 * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
    return pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract
```

with:

```python
def sample_rearing_params(z_head: float, rng: random.Random) -> Tuple[float, float, float]:
    """
    Size-relative parameters (unit-invariant).
    z_head is the rest-pose head height in local coords (your model ground is z=0).
    """
    pitch_scale = 1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.08, 0.08)  # ±8%

    # Scale paw motion to mouse size:
    paw_lift = 0.30 * z_head * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))
    paw_retract = 0.20 * z_head * (1.0 + rng.uniform(-0.15, 0.15))

    return pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract
```

### 2) Update the two call sites

You currently have:

```python
pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(rng)
```

Change to:

```python
pitch_scale, paw_lift, paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(z_head, rng)
```

And later, on entering rearing:

```python
beh.rear_pitch_scale, beh.rear_paw_lift, beh.rear_paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(rng)
```

Change to:

```python
beh.rear_pitch_scale, beh.rear_paw_lift, beh.rear_paw_retract = sample_rearing_params(z_head, rng)
```

That’s all.

## Why this matters for your cm → mm switch
Once rearing parameters scale off `z_head`, you can multiply all coordinates by 10 (cm→mm) and the rearing motion stays visually consistent without hunting down magic constants.

## If your `head.z` isn’t a good “size” proxy
If you ever change the model such that `head.z` is weird, a more robust size measure is the rest length of the main axis, e.g.:

```python
z_scale = float(np.linalg.norm(g.nodes[head] - g.nodes[tail_root]))
```

and use `z_scale` instead of `z_head`.

But given your current definition (reference point at z=0 below the head), `z_head` is perfectly fine.
