## `train_behavior.py`

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
import csv
import math
import os
import random
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np

# Deep learning
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader

# Classical baseline
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler
from sklearn.pipeline import Pipeline
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score, f1_score, classification_report


# ----------------------------
# Helpers
# ----------------------------

def nlabel(s: str) -> str:
    return s.strip().lower().replace(" ", "_")

def set_seed(seed: int) -> None:
    random.seed(seed)
    np.random.seed(seed)
    torch.manual_seed(seed)
    torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)  # no-op if no cuda


# ----------------------------
# Data structures
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class Run:
    name: str
    times: np.ndarray      # (T,)
    pos: np.ndarray        # (T,K,3)
    y: np.ndarray          # (T,)
    node_order: List[str]  # (K,)


def load_coords_3d_csv(path: str, node_order: Optional[List[str]] = None) -> Run:
    """
    Expects coords_3d.csv with columns:
      frame,time,behavior,node,x,y,z

    Returns a single Run.
    """
    if not os.path.exists(path):
        raise FileNotFoundError(path)

    rows = []
    with open(path, newline="", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        r = csv.DictReader(f)
        required = {"frame", "time", "behavior", "node", "x", "y", "z"}
        if not required.issubset(set(r.fieldnames or [])):
            raise ValueError(f"{path} missing required columns. Have: {r.fieldnames}")
        for row in r:
            rows.append(row)

    frames = sorted(set(int(rr["frame"]) for rr in rows))
    if not frames:
        raise ValueError(f"{path}: no frames")

    if node_order is None:
        node_order = sorted(set(nlabel(rr["node"]) for rr in rows))
    node_to_i = {n: i for i, n in enumerate(node_order)}

    T = len(frames)
    K = len(node_order)
    times = np.zeros((T,), dtype=np.float32)
    y = np.zeros((T,), dtype=np.int64)
    pos = np.zeros((T, K, 3), dtype=np.float32)

    by_frame: Dict[int, List[dict]] = {f: [] for f in frames}
    for rr in rows:
        by_frame[int(rr["frame"])].append(rr)

    for ti, fidx in enumerate(frames):
        fr = by_frame[fidx]
        times[ti] = float(fr[0]["time"])
        y[ti] = int(fr[0]["behavior"])
        for rr in fr:
            node = nlabel(rr["node"])
            if node not in node_to_i:
                continue
            j = node_to_i[node]
            pos[ti, j, 0] = float(rr["x"])
            pos[ti, j, 1] = float(rr["y"])
            pos[ti, j, 2] = float(rr["z"])

    return Run(name=os.path.basename(os.path.dirname(path)) or os.path.basename(path),
               times=times, pos=pos, y=y, node_order=node_order)


def body_frame_normalize(pos: np.ndarray,
                         node_order: List[str],
                         root: str = "tail_root",
                         head: str = "head",
                         eps: float = 1e-8) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    pos: (T,K,3) in world coords.
    output: body-centric coords:
      - translate so root at origin
      - rotate around z so forward (root->head) aligns to +x in xy-plane
    """
    root = nlabel(root); head = nlabel(head)
    idx = {n: i for i, n in enumerate(node_order)}
    if root not in idx or head not in idx:
        raise ValueError(f"root/head not found. root={root} head={head}")

    r = pos[:, idx[root], :]  # (T,3)
    h = pos[:, idx[head], :]  # (T,3)

    p = pos - r[:, None, :]   # translate

    fwd = h - r
    fwd_xy = fwd[:, :2]
    ang = np.arctan2(fwd_xy[:, 1], fwd_xy[:, 0])  # angle from +x
    ca = np.cos(-ang); sa = np.sin(-ang)

    out = p.copy()
    x = p[..., 0]; y = p[..., 1]
    out[..., 0] = ca[:, None] * x - sa[:, None] * y
    out[..., 1] = sa[:, None] * x + ca[:, None] * y
    # z unchanged
    return out


def make_features(pos_body: np.ndarray, use_vel: bool = True) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    pos_body: (T,K,3)
    returns X: (T,F) where F=3K (pos) or 6K (pos+vel)
    """
    T, K, _ = pos_body.shape
    p = pos_body.reshape(T, 3 * K)
    if not use_vel:
        return p
    v = np.zeros_like(p)
    v[1:] = p[1:] - p[:-1]
    return np.concatenate([p, v], axis=1)


# ----------------------------
# Windowing for deep models
# ----------------------------

class MultiRunWindowDataset(Dataset):
    """
    Builds windows (x[t:t+W], y[t:t+W]) across multiple runs.
    Splits by run: you pass a list of runs.
    """
    def __init__(self, runs: List[Run], window: int, stride: int,
                 root: str, head: str, use_vel: bool):
        self.window = window
        self.stride = stride
        self.samples: List[Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]] = []

        for run in runs:
            pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
            X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
            y = run.y
            if len(X) < window:
                continue
            for s in range(0, len(X) - window + 1, stride):
                self.samples.append((X[s:s+window], y[s:s+window]))

        if not self.samples:
            raise ValueError("No window samples created. Increase data or reduce window.")

    def __len__(self) -> int:
        return len(self.samples)

    def __getitem__(self, i: int):
        X, y = self.samples[i]
        return torch.tensor(X, dtype=torch.float32), torch.tensor(y, dtype=torch.long)


def predict_full_runs_deep(model: nn.Module, runs: List[Run], window: int, stride: int,
                           root: str, head: str, use_vel: bool,
                           device: torch.device) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    """
    Produce per-frame predictions for a list of runs by sliding a window and
    overlap-averaging logits.
    Returns (y_true_all, y_pred_all) concatenated across runs.
    """
    model.eval()
    y_true_all = []
    y_pred_all = []

    with torch.no_grad():
        for run in runs:
            pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
            X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
            T = len(X)
            logits_sum = np.zeros((T, 2), dtype=np.float64)
            counts = np.zeros((T,), dtype=np.float64)

            if T < window:
                # fall back: single chunk
                xb = torch.tensor(X[None, :, :], dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                logits = model(xb).cpu().numpy()[0]  # (T,2)
                logits_sum += logits
                counts += 1.0
            else:
                for s in range(0, T - window + 1, stride):
                    xb = torch.tensor(X[s:s+window][None, :, :], dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                    lg = model(xb).cpu().numpy()[0]  # (W,2)
                    logits_sum[s:s+window] += lg
                    counts[s:s+window] += 1.0
                # handle tail frames not covered (if stride>1)
                uncovered = counts < 0.5
                if uncovered.any():
                    xb = torch.tensor(X[None, :, :], dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                    lg = model(xb).cpu().numpy()[0]
                    logits_sum[uncovered] = lg[uncovered]
                    counts[uncovered] = 1.0

            logits_avg = logits_sum / counts[:, None]
            y_pred = logits_avg.argmax(axis=1).astype(np.int64)

            y_true_all.append(run.y.astype(np.int64))
            y_pred_all.append(y_pred)

    return np.concatenate(y_true_all), np.concatenate(y_pred_all)


# ----------------------------
# Models
# ----------------------------

class LSTMClassifier(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, in_dim: int, hidden: int = 128, layers: int = 2,
                 bidir: bool = True, dropout: float = 0.1):
        super().__init__()
        self.lstm = nn.LSTM(
            input_size=in_dim,
            hidden_size=hidden,
            num_layers=layers,
            batch_first=True,
            dropout=dropout if layers > 1 else 0.0,
            bidirectional=bidir,
        )
        out_dim = hidden * (2 if bidir else 1)
        self.head = nn.Linear(out_dim, 2)

    def forward(self, x):  # (B,T,F)
        z, _ = self.lstm(x)
        return self.head(z)  # (B,T,2)


class PositionalEncoding(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, d_model: int, max_len: int = 4096):
        super().__init__()
        pe = torch.zeros(max_len, d_model)
        pos = torch.arange(0, max_len).float().unsqueeze(1)
        div = torch.exp(torch.arange(0, d_model, 2).float() * (-math.log(10000.0) / d_model))
        pe[:, 0::2] = torch.sin(pos * div)
        pe[:, 1::2] = torch.cos(pos * div)
        self.register_buffer("pe", pe.unsqueeze(0))  # (1,max_len,d_model)

    def forward(self, x):
        return x + self.pe[:, :x.size(1), :]


class TransformerClassifier(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, in_dim: int, d_model: int = 128, nhead: int = 4,
                 layers: int = 4, ff: int = 256, dropout: float = 0.1):
        super().__init__()
        self.embed = nn.Linear(in_dim, d_model)
        self.pe = PositionalEncoding(d_model)
        enc_layer = nn.TransformerEncoderLayer(
            d_model=d_model,
            nhead=nhead,
            dim_feedforward=ff,
            dropout=dropout,
            batch_first=True,   # supported in modern torch
        )
        self.enc = nn.TransformerEncoder(enc_layer, num_layers=layers)
        self.head = nn.Linear(d_model, 2)

    def forward(self, x):
        z = self.embed(x)
        z = self.pe(z)
        z = self.enc(z)
        return self.head(z)


class xLSTMClassifier(nn.Module):
    """
    Uses the official 'xlstm' package's xLSTMBlockStack. citeturn2view0

    We keep it architecture-only (no LLM kernels). For portability, default backend='native'
    so it doesn't require CUDA kernel compilation. If you have a suitable NVIDIA GPU and
    want CUDA kernels, try backend='cuda' (may compile). citeturn2view0
    """
    def __init__(self, in_dim: int, d_model: int = 128, num_blocks: int = 4,
                 context_length: int = 256, backend: str = "native",
                 num_heads: int = 4, conv1d_kernel_size: int = 4):
        super().__init__()
        self.embed = nn.Linear(in_dim, d_model)

        try:
            from xlstm import (
                xLSTMBlockStack,
                xLSTMBlockStackConfig,
                mLSTMBlockConfig,
                mLSTMLayerConfig,
                sLSTMBlockConfig,
                sLSTMLayerConfig,
                FeedForwardConfig,
            )
        except Exception as e:
            raise RuntimeError(
                "xLSTM selected but 'xlstm' package is not installed.\n"
                "Install it with:\n"
                "  pip install xlstm\n"
                "or clone and editable-install:\n"
                "  git clone https://github.com/NX-AI/xlstm.git\n"
                "  cd xlstm && pip install -e .\n"
            ) from e

        # Config mirrors the README usage pattern. citeturn2view0
        cfg = xLSTMBlockStackConfig(
            mlstm_block=mLSTMBlockConfig(
                mlstm=mLSTMLayerConfig(
                    conv1d_kernel_size=conv1d_kernel_size,
                    qkv_proj_blocksize=4,
                    num_heads=num_heads,
                )
            ),
            slstm_block=sLSTMBlockConfig(
                slstm=sLSTMLayerConfig(
                    backend=backend,               # "native" or "cuda"
                    num_heads=num_heads,
                    conv1d_kernel_size=conv1d_kernel_size,
                    bias_init="powerlaw_blockdependent",
                ),
                feedforward=FeedForwardConfig(proj_factor=1.3, act_fn="gelu"),
            ),
            context_length=context_length,
            num_blocks=num_blocks,
            embedding_dim=d_model,
            slstm_at=[1],  # include sLSTM in at least one block (as in README example)
        )

        self.core = xLSTMBlockStack(cfg)
        self.head = nn.Linear(d_model, 2)

    def forward(self, x):
        z = self.embed(x)
        z = self.core(z)  # (B,T,d_model)
        return self.head(z)


# ----------------------------
# Classical baseline
# ----------------------------

def majority_smooth(y: np.ndarray, k: int) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Simple temporal smoothing: for each frame take majority vote in a +/- (k//2) window.
    k must be odd; if k<=1 returns y unchanged.
    """
    if k <= 1:
        return y.copy()
    if k % 2 == 0:
        raise ValueError("smooth-k must be odd")
    r = k // 2
    out = y.copy()
    for i in range(len(y)):
        a = max(0, i - r)
        b = min(len(y), i + r + 1)
        out[i] = 1 if (y[a:b].sum() > (b - a) / 2) else 0
    return out


def train_eval_logreg(train_runs: List[Run], test_runs: List[Run],
                      root: str, head: str, use_vel: bool,
                      C: float, smooth_k: int) -> None:
    # Build per-frame dataset
    Xtr_list, ytr_list = [], []
    Xte_list, yte_list = [], []

    for run in train_runs:
        pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
        X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
        Xtr_list.append(X)
        ytr_list.append(run.y)

    for run in test_runs:
        pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
        X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
        Xte_list.append(X)
        yte_list.append(run.y)

    Xtr = np.concatenate(Xtr_list, axis=0)
    ytr = np.concatenate(ytr_list, axis=0)
    Xte = np.concatenate(Xte_list, axis=0)
    yte = np.concatenate(yte_list, axis=0)

    clf = Pipeline([
        ("scaler", StandardScaler()),
        ("lr", LogisticRegression(
            C=C,
            max_iter=500,
            class_weight="balanced",  # helps if rearing is rarer
            solver="lbfgs",
        )),
    ])
    clf.fit(Xtr, ytr)
    yhat = clf.predict(Xte)

    # Optional smoothing: apply per-run to avoid cross-run window bleeding
    if smooth_k > 1:
        yhat_sm = []
        start = 0
        for run in test_runs:
            T = len(run.y)
            yhat_sm.append(majority_smooth(yhat[start:start+T], smooth_k))
            start += T
        yhat = np.concatenate(yhat_sm, axis=0)

    acc = accuracy_score(yte, yhat)
    f1 = f1_score(yte, yhat, pos_label=1)
    print(f"[baseline_logreg] acc={acc:.4f}  f1(rear)= {f1:.4f}")
    print(classification_report(yte, yhat, digits=4))


# ----------------------------
# Deep training loop
# ----------------------------

def train_deep(model: nn.Module,
               train_runs: List[Run],
               test_runs: List[Run],
               root: str, head: str, use_vel: bool,
               window: int, stride: int,
               batch: int, epochs: int, lr: float, wd: float,
               clip: float, device: torch.device) -> None:
    # Dataset
    ds_tr = MultiRunWindowDataset(train_runs, window=window, stride=stride,
                                  root=root, head=head, use_vel=use_vel)
    dl_tr = DataLoader(ds_tr, batch_size=batch, shuffle=True, drop_last=True, num_workers=0)

    # Optim / loss
    model.to(device)
    opt = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=lr, weight_decay=wd)
    crit = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()

    for epoch in range(1, epochs + 1):
        model.train()
        total_loss = 0.0
        for xb, yb in dl_tr:
            xb = xb.to(device)
            yb = yb.to(device)
            logits = model(xb)  # (B,W,2)
            loss = crit(logits.reshape(-1, 2), yb.reshape(-1))
            opt.zero_grad()
            loss.backward()
            nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(model.parameters(), clip)
            opt.step()
            total_loss += float(loss.item())

        # Evaluate on full test runs
        y_true, y_pred = predict_full_runs_deep(model, test_runs, window=window, stride=stride,
                                                root=root, head=head, use_vel=use_vel, device=device)
        acc = accuracy_score(y_true, y_pred)
        f1 = f1_score(y_true, y_pred, pos_label=1)
        print(f"[epoch {epoch:03d}] loss={total_loss/max(1,len(dl_tr)):.4f}  acc={acc:.4f}  f1(rear)={f1:.4f}")

    print(classification_report(y_true, y_pred, digits=4))


# ----------------------------
# Run splitting
# ----------------------------

def split_runs(runs: List[Run], test_frac: float, seed: int) -> Tuple[List[Run], List[Run]]:
    if len(runs) < 2:
        # fallback: time split inside single run is better than nothing, but not ideal
        r = runs[0]
        cut = int((1.0 - test_frac) * len(r.y))
        r1 = Run(name=r.name + "_train", times=r.times[:cut], pos=r.pos[:cut], y=r.y[:cut], node_order=r.node_order)
        r2 = Run(name=r.name + "_test", times=r.times[cut:], pos=r.pos[cut:], y=r.y[cut:], node_order=r.node_order)
        return [r1], [r2]

    rng = random.Random(seed)
    idx = list(range(len(runs)))
    rng.shuffle(idx)
    n_test = max(1, int(round(test_frac * len(runs))))
    test_idx = set(idx[:n_test])
    train_runs = [runs[i] for i in range(len(runs)) if i not in test_idx]
    test_runs = [runs[i] for i in range(len(runs)) if i in test_idx]
    return train_runs, test_runs


# ----------------------------
# Main
# ----------------------------

def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser("Behavior classifier: LSTM vs xLSTM vs Transformer + classical baseline")

    ap.add_argument("--coords-3d", nargs="+", required=True,
                    help="One or more coords_3d.csv paths (different runs).")
    ap.add_argument("--model", default="lstm",
                    choices=["baseline_logreg", "lstm", "transformer", "xlstm"])
    ap.add_argument("--seed", type=int, default=1)
    ap.add_argument("--cpu", action="store_true")

    # Preprocessing
    ap.add_argument("--root", default="tail_root")
    ap.add_argument("--head", default="head")
    ap.add_argument("--no-vel", action="store_true")

    # Splitting
    ap.add_argument("--test-frac", type=float, default=0.2)

    # Deep windowing
    ap.add_argument("--window", type=int, default=20)
    ap.add_argument("--stride", type=int, default=1)
    ap.add_argument("--batch", type=int, default=64)

    # Optim
    ap.add_argument("--epochs", type=int, default=30)
    ap.add_argument("--lr", type=float, default=3e-4)
    ap.add_argument("--wd", type=float, default=1e-4)
    ap.add_argument("--clip", type=float, default=1.0)

    # LSTM
    ap.add_argument("--hidden", type=int, default=128)
    ap.add_argument("--layers", type=int, default=2)
    ap.add_argument("--dropout", type=float, default=0.1)
    ap.add_argument("--no-bidir", action="store_true")

    # Transformer
    ap.add_argument("--d-model", type=int, default=128)
    ap.add_argument("--nhead", type=int, default=4)
    ap.add_argument("--ff", type=int, default=256)

    # xLSTM
    ap.add_argument("--xlstm-blocks", type=int, default=4)
    ap.add_argument("--xlstm-backend", default="native", choices=["native", "cuda"],
                    help="xLSTM sLSTM backend. 'native' avoids CUDA compilation. citeturn2view0")

    # Baseline
    ap.add_argument("--C", type=float, default=1.0, help="LogReg inverse regularization strength.")
    ap.add_argument("--smooth-k", type=int, default=1,
                    help="Odd window size for majority smoothing of baseline predictions (1 disables).")

    args = ap.parse_args()
    set_seed(args.seed)

    # Load runs
    runs = [load_coords_3d_csv(p) for p in args.coords_3d]
    # Ensure consistent node order across runs (use first run's order)
    base_order = runs[0].node_order
    for i in range(1, len(runs)):
        if runs[i].node_order != base_order:
            # reload with shared node order
            runs[i] = load_coords_3d_csv(args.coords_3d[i], node_order=base_order)

    train_runs, test_runs = split_runs(runs, test_frac=args.test_frac, seed=args.seed)
    print(f"runs: train={len(train_runs)} test={len(test_runs)}  (total={len(runs)})")

    use_vel = not args.no_vel

    if args.model == "baseline_logreg":
        if args.smooth_k > 1 and args.smooth_k % 2 == 0:
            raise ValueError("--smooth-k must be odd")
        train_eval_logreg(train_runs, test_runs,
                          root=args.root, head=args.head, use_vel=use_vel,
                          C=args.C, smooth_k=args.smooth_k)
        return

    # Deep models
    device = torch.device("cuda" if (torch.cuda.is_available() and not args.cpu) else "cpu")

    # Determine input dimension from first train run
    pb0 = body_frame_normalize(train_runs[0].pos, train_runs[0].node_order, root=args.root, head=args.head)
    X0 = make_features(pb0, use_vel=use_vel)
    in_dim = X0.shape[1]

    if args.model == "lstm":
        model = LSTMClassifier(
            in_dim=in_dim,
            hidden=args.hidden,
            layers=args.layers,
            bidir=not args.no_bidir,
            dropout=args.dropout,
        )
    elif args.model == "transformer":
        model = TransformerClassifier(
            in_dim=in_dim,
            d_model=args.d_model,
            nhead=args.nhead,
            layers=args.layers,
            ff=args.ff,
            dropout=args.dropout,
        )
    elif args.model == "xlstm":
        model = xLSTMClassifier(
            in_dim=in_dim,
            d_model=args.d_model,
            num_blocks=args.xlstm_blocks,
            context_length=args.window,
            backend=args.xlstm_backend,
            num_heads=args.nhead,
        )
    else:
        raise ValueError(args.model)

    train_deep(model,
               train_runs=train_runs,
               test_runs=test_runs,
               root=args.root, head=args.head, use_vel=use_vel,
               window=args.window, stride=args.stride,
               batch=args.batch, epochs=args.epochs, lr=args.lr, wd=args.wd,
               clip=args.clip, device=device)


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

## xLSTM: what you need on your side

### Minimal: pip install
The official repo explicitly supports installing as a Python package: `pip install xlstm` (or `pip install -e .` after cloning). citeturn2view0  
So you **do not need to clone** unless you want to modify internals.

Inside your conda env:
```bash
pip install xlstm
```

### About CUDA kernels
Their README notes optional CUDA kernels/backends for sLSTM and mentions GPU compute capability constraints and compilation considerations. citeturn2view0  
For your small sequence classification task, start with:

- `--xlstm-backend native` (no compilation, portable)

If you later want faster training/inference on an NVIDIA GPU, try `--xlstm-backend cuda` and follow their README if compilation issues appear. citeturn2view0

## B) Patch `train_behavior.py` to make real use of the GPU

### What we’ll add
- **AMP mixed precision** (`torch.cuda.amp.autocast` + `GradScaler`) → big speedup on 4090.
- **Pinned memory** + nonblocking transfers.
- **CuDNN benchmark**.
- Optional: **TF32** matmul acceleration for Ampere/Ada.

### 1) Add CLI flags
Add to `argparse`:

```python
ap.add_argument("--amp", action="store_true",
                help="Enable automatic mixed precision (recommended on NVIDIA GPUs).")
ap.add_argument("--tf32", action="store_true",
                help="Enable TF32 matmul on NVIDIA GPUs (faster, slight precision loss).")
ap.add_argument("--num-workers", type=int, default=2,
                help="Dataloader workers (increase if CPU allows).")
```

### 2) Set GPU performance knobs after device selection
In `main()` after `device = ...`:

```python
if device.type == "cuda":
    torch.backends.cudnn.benchmark = True
    if args.tf32:
        torch.backends.cuda.matmul.allow_tf32 = True
        torch.backends.cudnn.allow_tf32 = True
        # PyTorch 2.x: can also request higher matmul perf
        try:
            torch.set_float32_matmul_precision("high")
        except Exception:
            pass
```

### 3) Make dataloaders GPU-friendly
In `train_deep(...)`, when creating the DataLoader:

```python
dl_tr = DataLoader(
    ds_tr,
    batch_size=batch,
    shuffle=True,
    drop_last=True,
    num_workers=args.num_workers,
    pin_memory=(device.type == "cuda"),
    persistent_workers=(args.num_workers > 0),
)
```

(You’ll need to pass `args` or the worker count into `train_deep`; easiest is to add a `num_workers` arg parameter.)

### 4) Enable AMP in the training loop
Modify `train_deep(...)` signature to accept `use_amp: bool`, and inside:

```python
scaler = torch.cuda.amp.GradScaler(enabled=(use_amp and device.type == "cuda"))

for xb, yb in dl_tr:
    xb = xb.to(device, non_blocking=True)
    yb = yb.to(device, non_blocking=True)

    opt.zero_grad(set_to_none=True)

    with torch.cuda.amp.autocast(enabled=(use_amp and device.type == "cuda")):
        logits = model(xb)
        loss = crit(logits.reshape(-1, 2), yb.reshape(-1))

    scaler.scale(loss).backward()
    scaler.unscale_(opt)
    nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(model.parameters(), clip)
    scaler.step(opt)
    scaler.update()
```

That’s the critical GPU speed patch.

### 5) Make xLSTM default to CUDA backend when GPU is present
In your argparse defaults, change:

```python
ap.add_argument("--xlstm-backend", default="native", choices=["native", "cuda"], ...)
```

to:

```python
# keep default as "cuda" if you want to try kernels immediately
ap.add_argument("--xlstm-backend", default="cuda", choices=["native", "cuda"], ...)
```

And if CUDA backend fails on your system, run with:
```bash
--xlstm-backend native
```

## C) Minimal code diff summary (so you can apply quickly)

1) Add `--amp --tf32 --num-workers`.
2) Turn on `cudnn.benchmark`, optionally TF32.
3) Dataloader: `pin_memory=True`, `persistent_workers=True`.
4) Training step uses AMP + `GradScaler`.

Your script already uses CUDA if available; this makes it **fast** on the 4090.

User: Yes, please provide the fully updated train_behavior.py.

Assistant: ```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
from __future__ import annotations

import argparse
import csv
import math
import os
import random
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple, Optional

import numpy as np

# Deep learning
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader

# Classical baseline
from sklearn.linear_model import LogisticRegression
from sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler
from sklearn.pipeline import Pipeline
from sklearn.metrics import accuracy_score, f1_score, classification_report


# ----------------------------
# Helpers
# ----------------------------

def nlabel(s: str) -> str:
    return s.strip().lower().replace(" ", "_")


def set_seed(seed: int) -> None:
    random.seed(seed)
    np.random.seed(seed)
    torch.manual_seed(seed)
    torch.cuda.manual_seed_all(seed)  # no-op if no cuda


# ----------------------------
# Data structures
# ----------------------------

@dataclass
class Run:
    name: str
    times: np.ndarray      # (T,)
    pos: np.ndarray        # (T,K,3)
    y: np.ndarray          # (T,)
    node_order: List[str]  # (K,)


def load_coords_3d_csv(path: str, node_order: Optional[List[str]] = None) -> Run:
    """
    Expects coords_3d.csv with columns:
      frame,time,behavior,node,x,y,z

    Returns a single Run.
    """
    if not os.path.exists(path):
        raise FileNotFoundError(path)

    rows = []
    with open(path, newline="", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        r = csv.DictReader(f)
        required = {"frame", "time", "behavior", "node", "x", "y", "z"}
        if not required.issubset(set(r.fieldnames or [])):
            raise ValueError(f"{path} missing required columns. Have: {r.fieldnames}")
        for row in r:
            rows.append(row)

    frames = sorted(set(int(rr["frame"]) for rr in rows))
    if not frames:
        raise ValueError(f"{path}: no frames")

    if node_order is None:
        node_order = sorted(set(nlabel(rr["node"]) for rr in rows))
    node_to_i = {n: i for i, n in enumerate(node_order)}

    T = len(frames)
    K = len(node_order)
    times = np.zeros((T,), dtype=np.float32)
    y = np.zeros((T,), dtype=np.int64)
    pos = np.zeros((T, K, 3), dtype=np.float32)

    by_frame: Dict[int, List[dict]] = {f: [] for f in frames}
    for rr in rows:
        by_frame[int(rr["frame"])].append(rr)

    for ti, fidx in enumerate(frames):
        fr = by_frame[fidx]
        times[ti] = float(fr[0]["time"])
        y[ti] = int(fr[0]["behavior"])
        for rr in fr:
            node = nlabel(rr["node"])
            if node not in node_to_i:
                continue
            j = node_to_i[node]
            pos[ti, j, 0] = float(rr["x"])
            pos[ti, j, 1] = float(rr["y"])
            pos[ti, j, 2] = float(rr["z"])

    return Run(
        name=os.path.basename(os.path.dirname(path)) or os.path.basename(path),
        times=times,
        pos=pos,
        y=y,
        node_order=node_order,
    )


def body_frame_normalize(
    pos: np.ndarray,
    node_order: List[str],
    root: str = "tail_root",
    head: str = "head",
) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    pos: (T,K,3) in world/cage coords.
    output: body-centric coords:
      - translate so root at origin
      - rotate around z so forward (root->head) aligns to +x in xy-plane
    """
    root = nlabel(root)
    head = nlabel(head)
    idx = {n: i for i, n in enumerate(node_order)}
    if root not in idx or head not in idx:
        raise ValueError(f"root/head not found. root={root} head={head}")

    r = pos[:, idx[root], :]  # (T,3)
    h = pos[:, idx[head], :]  # (T,3)

    p = pos - r[:, None, :]   # translate

    fwd = h - r
    ang = np.arctan2(fwd[:, 1], fwd[:, 0])  # angle from +x
    ca = np.cos(-ang)
    sa = np.sin(-ang)

    out = p.copy()
    x = p[..., 0]
    y = p[..., 1]
    out[..., 0] = ca[:, None] * x - sa[:, None] * y
    out[..., 1] = sa[:, None] * x + ca[:, None] * y
    # z unchanged
    return out


def make_features(pos_body: np.ndarray, use_vel: bool = True) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    pos_body: (T,K,3)
    returns X: (T,F) where F=3K (pos) or 6K (pos+vel)
    """
    T, K, _ = pos_body.shape
    p = pos_body.reshape(T, 3 * K)
    if not use_vel:
        return p
    v = np.zeros_like(p)
    v[1:] = p[1:] - p[:-1]
    return np.concatenate([p, v], axis=1)


# ----------------------------
# Windowing for deep models
# ----------------------------

class MultiRunWindowDataset(Dataset):
    """
    Builds windows (x[t:t+W], y[t:t+W]) across multiple runs.
    Split by run happens outside this dataset.
    """
    def __init__(
        self,
        runs: List[Run],
        window: int,
        stride: int,
        root: str,
        head: str,
        use_vel: bool,
    ):
        self.window = window
        self.stride = stride
        self.samples: List[Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]] = []

        for run in runs:
            pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
            X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
            y = run.y
            if len(X) < window:
                continue
            for s in range(0, len(X) - window + 1, stride):
                self.samples.append((X[s:s + window], y[s:s + window]))

        if not self.samples:
            raise ValueError("No window samples created. Increase data or reduce window.")

    def __len__(self) -> int:
        return len(self.samples)

    def __getitem__(self, i: int):
        X, y = self.samples[i]
        return torch.tensor(X, dtype=torch.float32), torch.tensor(y, dtype=torch.long)


def predict_full_runs_deep(
    model: nn.Module,
    runs: List[Run],
    window: int,
    stride: int,
    root: str,
    head: str,
    use_vel: bool,
    device: torch.device,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, np.ndarray]:
    """
    Per-frame predictions for full runs by sliding window and overlap-averaging logits.
    Returns concatenated (y_true_all, y_pred_all).
    """
    model.eval()
    y_true_all = []
    y_pred_all = []

    with torch.no_grad():
        for run in runs:
            pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
            X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
            T = len(X)
            logits_sum = np.zeros((T, 2), dtype=np.float64)
            counts = np.zeros((T,), dtype=np.float64)

            if T < window:
                xb = torch.tensor(X[None, :, :], dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                logits = model(xb).detach().cpu().numpy()[0]  # (T,2)
                logits_sum += logits
                counts += 1.0
            else:
                for s in range(0, T - window + 1, stride):
                    xb = torch.tensor(X[s:s + window][None, :, :], dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                    lg = model(xb).detach().cpu().numpy()[0]  # (W,2)
                    logits_sum[s:s + window] += lg
                    counts[s:s + window] += 1.0

                uncovered = counts < 0.5
                if uncovered.any():
                    xb = torch.tensor(X[None, :, :], dtype=torch.float32, device=device)
                    lg = model(xb).detach().cpu().numpy()[0]
                    logits_sum[uncovered] = lg[uncovered]
                    counts[uncovered] = 1.0

            logits_avg = logits_sum / counts[:, None]
            y_pred = logits_avg.argmax(axis=1).astype(np.int64)

            y_true_all.append(run.y.astype(np.int64))
            y_pred_all.append(y_pred)

    return np.concatenate(y_true_all), np.concatenate(y_pred_all)


# ----------------------------
# Models
# ----------------------------

class LSTMClassifier(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, in_dim: int, hidden: int = 128, layers: int = 2,
                 bidir: bool = True, dropout: float = 0.1):
        super().__init__()
        self.lstm = nn.LSTM(
            input_size=in_dim,
            hidden_size=hidden,
            num_layers=layers,
            batch_first=True,
            dropout=dropout if layers > 1 else 0.0,
            bidirectional=bidir,
        )
        out_dim = hidden * (2 if bidir else 1)
        self.head = nn.Linear(out_dim, 2)

    def forward(self, x):  # (B,T,F)
        z, _ = self.lstm(x)
        return self.head(z)  # (B,T,2)


class PositionalEncoding(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, d_model: int, max_len: int = 4096):
        super().__init__()
        pe = torch.zeros(max_len, d_model)
        pos = torch.arange(0, max_len).float().unsqueeze(1)
        div = torch.exp(torch.arange(0, d_model, 2).float() * (-math.log(10000.0) / d_model))
        pe[:, 0::2] = torch.sin(pos * div)
        pe[:, 1::2] = torch.cos(pos * div)
        self.register_buffer("pe", pe.unsqueeze(0))  # (1,max_len,d_model)

    def forward(self, x):
        return x + self.pe[:, :x.size(1), :]


class TransformerClassifier(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, in_dim: int, d_model: int = 128, nhead: int = 4,
                 layers: int = 4, ff: int = 256, dropout: float = 0.1):
        super().__init__()
        self.embed = nn.Linear(in_dim, d_model)
        self.pe = PositionalEncoding(d_model)
        enc_layer = nn.TransformerEncoderLayer(
            d_model=d_model,
            nhead=nhead,
            dim_feedforward=ff,
            dropout=dropout,
            batch_first=True,
        )
        self.enc = nn.TransformerEncoder(enc_layer, num_layers=layers)
        self.head = nn.Linear(d_model, 2)

    def forward(self, x):
        z = self.embed(x)
        z = self.pe(z)
        z = self.enc(z)
        return self.head(z)


class xLSTMClassifier(nn.Module):
    """
    Requires: pip install xlstm
    Uses xLSTMBlockStack with a config similar to the official README example.
    """
    def __init__(
        self,
        in_dim: int,
        d_model: int = 128,
        num_blocks: int = 4,
        context_length: int = 256,
        backend: str = "native",
        num_heads: int = 4,
        conv1d_kernel_size: int = 4,
    ):
        super().__init__()
        self.embed = nn.Linear(in_dim, d_model)

        try:
            from xlstm import (
                xLSTMBlockStack,
                xLSTMBlockStackConfig,
                mLSTMBlockConfig,
                mLSTMLayerConfig,
                sLSTMBlockConfig,
                sLSTMLayerConfig,
                FeedForwardConfig,
            )
        except Exception as e:
            raise RuntimeError(
                "xLSTM selected but 'xlstm' package is not installed.\n"
                "Install in your environment with:\n"
                "  pip install xlstm\n"
                "If you want editable install:\n"
                "  git clone https://github.com/NX-AI/xlstm.git\n"
                "  cd xlstm && pip install -e .\n"
            ) from e

        cfg = xLSTMBlockStackConfig(
            mlstm_block=mLSTMBlockConfig(
                mlstm=mLSTMLayerConfig(
                    conv1d_kernel_size=conv1d_kernel_size,
                    qkv_proj_blocksize=4,
                    num_heads=num_heads,
                )
            ),
            slstm_block=sLSTMBlockConfig(
                slstm=sLSTMLayerConfig(
                    backend=backend,  # "native" or "cuda"
                    num_heads=num_heads,
                    conv1d_kernel_size=conv1d_kernel_size,
                    bias_init="powerlaw_blockdependent",
                ),
                feedforward=FeedForwardConfig(proj_factor=1.3, act_fn="gelu"),
            ),
            context_length=context_length,
            num_blocks=num_blocks,
            embedding_dim=d_model,
            slstm_at=[1],
        )

        self.core = xLSTMBlockStack(cfg)
        self.head = nn.Linear(d_model, 2)

    def forward(self, x):
        z = self.embed(x)
        z = self.core(z)
        return self.head(z)


# ----------------------------
# Classical baseline
# ----------------------------

def majority_smooth(y: np.ndarray, k: int) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Majority vote in +/- (k//2) window. k must be odd; k<=1 disables.
    """
    if k <= 1:
        return y.copy()
    if k % 2 == 0:
        raise ValueError("smooth-k must be odd")
    r = k // 2
    out = y.copy()
    for i in range(len(y)):
        a = max(0, i - r)
        b = min(len(y), i + r + 1)
        out[i] = 1 if (y[a:b].sum() > (b - a) / 2) else 0
    return out


def train_eval_logreg(
    train_runs: List[Run],
    test_runs: List[Run],
    root: str,
    head: str,
    use_vel: bool,
    C: float,
    smooth_k: int,
) -> None:
    # Build per-frame dataset
    Xtr_list, ytr_list = [], []
    Xte_list, yte_list = [], []

    for run in train_runs:
        pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
        X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
        Xtr_list.append(X)
        ytr_list.append(run.y)

    for run in test_runs:
        pb = body_frame_normalize(run.pos, run.node_order, root=root, head=head)
        X = make_features(pb, use_vel=use_vel)
        Xte_list.append(X)
        yte_list.append(run.y)

    Xtr = np.concatenate(Xtr_list, axis=0)
    ytr = np.concatenate(ytr_list, axis=0)
    Xte = np.concatenate(Xte_list, axis=0)
    yte = np.concatenate(yte_list, axis=0)

    clf = Pipeline([
        ("scaler", StandardScaler()),
        ("lr", LogisticRegression(
            C=C,
            max_iter=1000,
            class_weight="balanced",
            solver="lbfgs",
        )),
    ])
    clf.fit(Xtr, ytr)
    yhat = clf.predict(Xte)

    # Optional smoothing per-run (avoid bleeding across runs)
    if smooth_k > 1:
        yhat_sm = []
        start = 0
        for run in test_runs:
            T = len(run.y)
            yhat_sm.append(majority_smooth(yhat[start:start + T], smooth_k))
            start += T
        yhat = np.concatenate(yhat_sm, axis=0)

    acc = accuracy_score(yte, yhat)
    f1 = f1_score(yte, yhat, pos_label=1)
    print(f"[baseline_logreg] acc={acc:.4f}  f1(rear)={f1:.4f}")
    print(classification_report(yte, yhat, digits=4))


# ----------------------------
# Deep training loop (GPU optimized)
# ----------------------------

def train_deep(
    model: nn.Module,
    train_runs: List[Run],
    test_runs: List[Run],
    root: str,
    head: str,
    use_vel: bool,
    window: int,
    stride: int,
    batch: int,
    epochs: int,
    lr: float,
    wd: float,
    clip: float,
    device: torch.device,
    use_amp: bool,
    num_workers: int,
) -> None:
    ds_tr = MultiRunWindowDataset(
        train_runs, window=window, stride=stride, root=root, head=head, use_vel=use_vel
    )
    dl_tr = DataLoader(
        ds_tr,
        batch_size=batch,
        shuffle=True,
        drop_last=True,
        num_workers=num_workers,
        pin_memory=(device.type == "cuda"),
        persistent_workers=(num_workers > 0),
    )

    model.to(device)
    opt = torch.optim.AdamW(model.parameters(), lr=lr, weight_decay=wd)
    crit = nn.CrossEntropyLoss()

    scaler = torch.cuda.amp.GradScaler(enabled=(use_amp and device.type == "cuda"))
    amp_enabled = (use_amp and device.type == "cuda")

    for epoch in range(1, epochs + 1):
        model.train()
        total_loss = 0.0

        for xb, yb in dl_tr:
            xb = xb.to(device, non_blocking=True)
            yb = yb.to(device, non_blocking=True)

            opt.zero_grad(set_to_none=True)

            with torch.cuda.amp.autocast(enabled=amp_enabled):
                logits = model(xb)  # (B,W,2)
                loss = crit(logits.reshape(-1, 2), yb.reshape(-1))

            scaler.scale(loss).backward()
            scaler.unscale_(opt)
            nn.utils.clip_grad_norm_(model.parameters(), clip)
            scaler.step(opt)
            scaler.update()

            total_loss += float(loss.item())

        # Evaluate on full test runs
        y_true, y_pred = predict_full_runs_deep(
            model,
            test_runs,
            window=window,
            stride=stride,
            root=root,
            head=head,
            use_vel=use_vel,
            device=device,
        )
        acc = accuracy_score(y_true, y_pred)
        f1 = f1_score(y_true, y_pred, pos_label=1)
        avg_loss = total_loss / max(1, len(dl_tr))
        print(f"[epoch {epoch:03d}] loss={avg_loss:.4f}  acc={acc:.4f}  f1(rear)={f1:.4f}")

    print(classification_report(y_true, y_pred, digits=4))


# ----------------------------
# Run splitting
# ----------------------------

def split_runs(runs: List[Run], test_frac: float, seed: int) -> Tuple[List[Run], List[Run]]:
    """
    Preferred: split by run (seed) to avoid leakage.
    If only one run is provided, falls back to time split.
    """
    if len(runs) < 2:
        r = runs[0]
        cut = int((1.0 - test_frac) * len(r.y))
        r1 = Run(name=r.name + "_train", times=r.times[:cut], pos=r.pos[:cut], y=r.y[:cut], node_order=r.node_order)
        r2 = Run(name=r.name + "_test", times=r.times[cut:], pos=r.pos[cut:], y=r.y[cut:], node_order=r.node_order)
        return [r1], [r2]

    rng = random.Random(seed)
    idx = list(range(len(runs)))
    rng.shuffle(idx)
    n_test = max(1, int(round(test_frac * len(runs))))
    test_idx = set(idx[:n_test])
    train_runs = [runs[i] for i in range(len(runs)) if i not in test_idx]
    test_runs = [runs[i] for i in range(len(runs)) if i in test_idx]
    return train_runs, test_runs


# ----------------------------
# Main
# ----------------------------

def main():
    ap = argparse.ArgumentParser("Behavior classifier: baseline vs LSTM vs xLSTM vs Transformer (GPU-ready)")

    ap.add_argument("--coords-3d", nargs="+", required=True,
                    help="One or more coords_3d.csv paths (different simulation runs).")
    ap.add_argument("--model", default="lstm",
                    choices=["baseline_logreg", "lstm", "transformer", "xlstm"])
    ap.add_argument("--seed", type=int, default=1)
    ap.add_argument("--cpu", action="store_true")

    # GPU performance switches
    ap.add_argument("--amp", action="store_true",
                    help="Enable automatic mixed precision (recommended on NVIDIA GPUs).")
    ap.add_argument("--tf32", action="store_true",
                    help="Enable TF32 matmul on NVIDIA GPUs (faster, slight precision loss).")
    ap.add_argument("--num-workers", type=int, default=2,
                    help="DataLoader workers (increase if CPU allows).")

    # Preprocessing
    ap.add_argument("--root", default="tail_root")
    ap.add_argument("--head", default="head")
    ap.add_argument("--no-vel", action="store_true")

    # Splitting
    ap.add_argument("--test-frac", type=float, default=0.2)

    # Deep windowing
    ap.add_argument("--window", type=int, default=20)
    ap.add_argument("--stride", type=int, default=1)
    ap.add_argument("--batch", type=int, default=64)

    # Optim
    ap.add_argument("--epochs", type=int, default=30)
    ap.add_argument("--lr", type=float, default=3e-4)
    ap.add_argument("--wd", type=float, default=1e-4)
    ap.add_argument("--clip", type=float, default=1.0)

    # LSTM
    ap.add_argument("--hidden", type=int, default=128)
    ap.add_argument("--layers", type=int, default=2)
    ap.add_argument("--dropout", type=float, default=0.1)
    ap.add_argument("--no-bidir", action="store_true")

    # Transformer / xLSTM shared-ish
    ap.add_argument("--d-model", type=int, default=128)
    ap.add_argument("--nhead", type=int, default=4)
    ap.add_argument("--ff", type=int, default=256)

    # xLSTM
    ap.add_argument("--xlstm-blocks", type=int, default=4)
    ap.add_argument("--xlstm-backend", default="cuda", choices=["native", "cuda"],
                    help="xLSTM sLSTM backend. Use 'native' if CUDA backend fails to compile.")
    ap.add_argument("--xlstm-kernel", type=int, default=4)

    # Baseline
    ap.add_argument("--C", type=float, default=1.0, help="LogReg inverse regularization strength.")
    ap.add_argument("--smooth-k", type=int, default=1,
                    help="Odd window size for majority smoothing of baseline predictions (1 disables).")

    args = ap.parse_args()
    set_seed(args.seed)

    # Device selection
    device = torch.device("cuda" if (torch.cuda.is_available() and not args.cpu) else "cpu")
    print("device:", device)
    if device.type == "cuda":
        print("gpu:", torch.cuda.get_device_name(0))
        # Better cuDNN autotuning for fixed shapes
        torch.backends.cudnn.benchmark = True
        if args.tf32:
            torch.backends.cuda.matmul.allow_tf32 = True
            torch.backends.cudnn.allow_tf32 = True
            try:
                torch.set_float32_matmul_precision("high")
            except Exception:
                pass

    # Load runs
    runs = [load_coords_3d_csv(p) for p in args.coords_3d]

    # Ensure consistent node order across runs
    base_order = runs[0].node_order
    for i in range(1, len(runs)):
        if runs[i].node_order != base_order:
            runs[i] = load_coords_3d_csv(args.coords_3d[i], node_order=base_order)

    train_runs, test_runs = split_runs(runs, test_frac=args.test_frac, seed=args.seed)
    print(f"runs: train={len(train_runs)} test={len(test_runs)} total={len(runs)}")

    use_vel = not args.no_vel

    # Baseline
    if args.model == "baseline_logreg":
        if args.smooth_k > 1 and args.smooth_k % 2 == 0:
            raise ValueError("--smooth-k must be odd")
        train_eval_logreg(
            train_runs, test_runs,
            root=args.root, head=args.head, use_vel=use_vel,
            C=args.C, smooth_k=args.smooth_k,
        )
        return

    # Determine input dimension
    pb0 = body_frame_normalize(train_runs[0].pos, train_runs[0].node_order, root=args.root, head=args.head)
    X0 = make_features(pb0, use_vel=use_vel)
    in_dim = X0.shape[1]

    # Model selection
    if args.model == "lstm":
        model = LSTMClassifier(
            in_dim=in_dim,
            hidden=args.hidden,
            layers=args.layers,
            bidir=not args.no_bidir,
            dropout=args.dropout,
        )
    elif args.model == "transformer":
        model = TransformerClassifier(
            in_dim=in_dim,
            d_model=args.d_model,
            nhead=args.nhead,
            layers=args.layers,
            ff=args.ff,
            dropout=args.dropout,
        )
    elif args.model == "xlstm":
        model = xLSTMClassifier(
            in_dim=in_dim,
            d_model=args.d_model,
            num_blocks=args.xlstm_blocks,
            context_length=args.window,
            backend=args.xlstm_backend,
            num_heads=args.nhead,
            conv1d_kernel_size=args.xlstm_kernel,
        )
    else:
        raise ValueError(args.model)

    # Train
    train_deep(
        model,
        train_runs=train_runs,
        test_runs=test_runs,
        root=args.root,
        head=args.head,
        use_vel=use_vel,
        window=args.window,
        stride=args.stride,
        batch=args.batch,
        epochs=args.epochs,
        lr=args.lr,
        wd=args.wd,
        clip=args.clip,
        device=device,
        use_amp=args.amp,
        num_workers=args.num_workers,
    )


if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```bash

```

2) Install xLSTM:
```bash
pip install xlstm
```

```bash

  --model transformer --epochs 30 --window 20 --amp --tf32 --num-workers 4
```

4) Try xLSTM CUDA backend; if it errors (kernel compile issues), fall back to `native`:
```bash
python train_behavior.py --coords-3d out1/coords_3d.csv out2/coords_3d.csv out3/coords_3d.csv \
  --model xlstm --epochs 30 --window 20 --amp --tf32 --num-workers 4 --xlstm-backend cuda
# fallback:
# ... --xlstm-backend native
```

Assistant: On **Ubuntu 22.04** with an NVIDIA driver that reports **CUDA 12.4 / 12.8** in `nvidia-smi`, you’re in good shape. The key point is:

**PyTorch ships its own CUDA runtime** (when you install the CUDA-enabled build), and it only needs your **driver** to be new enough. You do *not* need a matching system-wide CUDA toolkit for normal training.

### 1) Check what you actually have right now
Run:

```bash
nvidia-smi
```

Look at the top line:

- **Driver Version:** e.g. 550.xx
- **CUDA Version:** e.g. 12.4 (this is what the driver supports)

Also check in your conda env:

```bash
python -c "import torch; print('torch', torch.__version__); print('cuda available', torch.cuda.is_available()); print('torch cuda', torch.version.cuda); print('gpu', torch.cuda.get_device_name(0) if torch.cuda.is_available() else None)"
```

If `cuda available` is `False`, you installed a CPU-only PyTorch build.

---

## Recommended installation (works with driver CUDA 12.4+)
This is the most reliable approach on Linux:

```bash
conda install -y pytorch torchvision torchaudio pytorch-cuda=12.1 -c pytorch -c nvidia
```

Why `12.1` even if your driver says 12.4/12.8?
- Because `pytorch-cuda=12.1` is widely supported and stable.
- Your driver reporting 12.4/12.8 is **new enough** (drivers are backward compatible for CUDA runtime).

Then re-check:

```bash
python -c "import torch; print(torch.cuda.is_available(), torch.version.cuda, torch.cuda.get_device_name(0))"
```

---

## If you hit “version conflict” issues
Sometimes conda will try to mix CUDA runtimes from conda-forge vs pytorch/nvidia channels.

Two strong remedies:

### Remedy A: Install PyTorch CUDA stack first, then everything else
In a fresh env:
```bash
conda create -n mouse-sim-gpu -c pytorch -c nvidia -c conda-forge python=3.11 pytorch torchvision torchaudio pytorch-cuda=12.1
conda activate mouse-sim-gpu
conda install -c conda-forge numpy scipy pillow tqdm opencv imageio imageio-ffmpeg scikit-learn trimesh pyrender pyglet pyopengl
pip install xlstm
```

### Remedy B: If you keep the existing env, “prune” and reinstall CUDA pieces
```bash
conda activate <your_env>
conda remove -y pytorch torchvision torchaudio cudatoolkit cuda-version pytorch-cuda
conda install -y pytorch torchvision torchaudio pytorch-cuda=12.1 -c pytorch -c nvidia
```

---

## About xLSTM CUDA backend on your machine
Your training will already be GPU-fast with PyTorch + AMP. xLSTM’s **`backend="cuda"`** may try to use custom CUDA kernels; that can require a compiler toolchain (and sometimes `nvcc`).

If `--xlstm-backend cuda` fails, just use:
```bash
--xlstm-backend native
```

You still run on GPU for most ops; you just skip custom kernels.

If you *do* want to try compiling kernels, add a toolkit in the env:
```bash
conda install -c nvidia cuda-toolkit=12.1
```
(Only necessary if compilation is required; many users never need this.)

---

## Once CUDA works, run training with your GPU knobs
Example:
```bash
python train_behavior.py --coords-3d out1/coords_3d.csv out2/coords_3d.csv out3/coords_3d.csv \
  --model transformer --epochs 30 --window 20 --amp --tf32 --num-workers 4
```

```yaml
name: mouse_sim
channels:
  - pytorch
  - nvidia
  - conda-forge
dependencies:
  - python=3.11
  - pip
```

Assistant: All-black frames from `pyrender` almost always mean **the mesh never contributes fragments** (camera looks the wrong way / object behind camera / everything is back-face culled / GL context not actually rendering). Given your run “completed” and wrote MP4s, the two most likely culprits are:

## 1) Camera convention mismatch (CV vs OpenGL) → object behind camera
`pyrender` uses an **OpenGL-style camera**: in camera space it looks along **−Z** with **+Y up**. Many pinhole “vision” pipelines (and it’s very plausible `mouse-sim.py` is one) use **+Z forward** and often **+Y down**.

If you export `R,t` from Mouse 1 in a CV convention and then feed them into `pyrender` without converting, the mesh can end up entirely behind the camera → black.

### Fix: apply a CV→OpenGL axis flip before inverting pose
In `mouse_deform_render.py`, modify `world_to_cam_to_pose` like this:

```python
def world_to_cam_to_pose(R_wc: np.ndarray, t_wc: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    cameras.json stores world->cam as Pc = R_wc*Pw + t_wc in a CV convention.
    Convert to OpenGL camera convention used by pyrender (x right, y up, -z forward),
    then return cam->world pose.
    """
    # CV (x right, y down, z forward) -> GL (x right, y up, z backward)
    cv_to_gl = np.diag([1.0, -1.0, -1.0])

    R_wc_gl = cv_to_gl @ R_wc
    t_wc_gl = cv_to_gl @ t_wc

    R_cw = R_wc_gl.T
    t_cw = -R_cw @ t_wc_gl

    pose = np.eye(4, dtype=np.float64)
    pose[:3, :3] = R_cw
    pose[:3, 3] = t_cw
    return pose
```

This single change fixes “black screen” in a *lot* of CV→OpenGL integrations.

**Quick diagnostic without changing rendering:** print where the object is in camera coords. After you compute a deformed mesh for a frame, compute its bbox center `Cw`, then `Cc = R_wc @ Cw + t_wc`. If `Cc[2]` is negative/positive depends on your convention; the important part is whether it’s “in front” according to the convention you used when projecting keypoints in Mouse 1. If it’s consistently the “wrong sign”, you’ve found the issue.

## 2) Back-face culling (winding/normals) → everything culled
If the OBJ has reversed face winding relative to the camera after deformation/transform, OpenGL can cull every triangle. Result: black, even though the camera is right.

### Fast test: disable face culling in the render call
In `mouse_deform_render.py`:

```python
from pyrender import RenderFlags
color, _depth = renderer.render(scene, flags=RenderFlags.SKIP_CULL_FACES)
```

If that makes the mesh appear, then you’ve confirmed culling is the problem. You can then either keep this flag, or make materials double-sided.

## 3) Wrong mesh-nodes coordinate system (less likely in your case, but check)
You uploaded two node files that are clearly **axis-permuted** versions of each other:

- `mouse_mesh_nodes.txt` has e.g. `head 0 28 26` fileciteturn3file0  
- `mouse3_mesh.txt` has `head 26 0 28` fileciteturn3file1  

That’s basically `(x',y',z') = (z,x,y)`.

For the deform renderer, `--mesh-nodes` **must be in the OBJ’s native coordinate system** (i.e., consistent with the actual vertex coordinates), otherwise the deformation can throw the mesh somewhere nonsensical. You *said* you’re using the OBJ-derived nodes file, so you’re likely fine here—just calling out that mixing these two will absolutely break things.

## 4) Offscreen OpenGL backend issue (headless/driver quirks)  
Less likely because you got no exception, but still possible on some setups: context “works” but renders black.

Try once:

```bash
export PYOPENGL_PLATFORM=egl
python mouse_deform_render.py ...
```

(If you’re on a normal desktop session, the camera-convention mismatch is still the top suspect.)

Assistant: Thanks — that camera dump is exactly what’s needed, and it strongly indicates the root cause.

### What your `R,t` mean (and why pyrender shows black)
Your camera is stored in a **computer-vision / OpenCV convention**:

\[
P_c = R_{wc} P_w + t_{wc}
\]

with **camera +Z pointing forward**.

You can verify that from your numbers:

- From your `R,t`, the camera center is  
  \[
  C = -R^T t = (200,\,-388.516,\,150)
  \]
  which matches your `pos_world` (you truncated `z`, but it’s 150).  
- If you project the cage center (e.g. \(P_w=(200,200,0)\)) you get a **positive** camera z (≈ 600), i.e. “in front” in CV coordinates.

However, **pyrender/OpenGL uses the opposite convention**: the camera looks along **−Z** (and +Y is up). If you feed an OpenCV-style `R,t` straight into pyrender, the whole scene ends up effectively **behind the camera**, and you get perfectly valid renders of… nothing → **all-black frames**.

So this is not a texture issue; your texture chain is already confirmed working.

---

## Fix: convert CV camera extrinsics to OpenGL before building the pose
In `mouse_deform_render.py`, replace your `world_to_cam_to_pose` with this:

```python
def world_to_cam_to_pose(R_wc: np.ndarray, t_wc: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Convert world->cam extrinsics in OpenCV convention (x right, y down, z forward)
    to an OpenGL/pyrender camera pose (cam->world, looking down -Z, y up).
    """
    # CV -> GL axis flip (keeps x, flips y and z)
    cv_to_gl = np.diag([1.0, -1.0, -1.0])

    R_wc_gl = cv_to_gl @ R_wc
    t_wc_gl = cv_to_gl @ t_wc

    # invert world->cam to cam->world pose
    R_cw = R_wc_gl.T
    t_cw = -R_cw @ t_wc_gl

    pose = np.eye(4, dtype=np.float64)
    pose[:3, :3] = R_cw
    pose[:3, 3] = t_cw
    return pose
```

Run again. In most CV→pyrender pipelines, this single change fixes “all black”.

---

## Secondary quick test: disable face culling (in case winding/normals are flipped)
If after the camera fix you still see black, the next most common cause is **back-face culling**. Test it by rendering with:

```python
from pyrender import RenderFlags
color, _depth = renderer.render(scene, flags=RenderFlags.SKIP_CULL_FACES)
```

If the mesh appears then, it’s a culling/winding issue (and you can keep that flag or make materials double-sided).

---

## Why I’m confident the camera-convention mismatch is *the* issue here
Your `R` has first row ≈ `[1,0,0]`, and the third row is mostly world +Y (≈ 0.996). That is exactly what you’d expect for a “front camera” positioned at **negative world y** looking toward **positive world y**, when **camera z is forward** (OpenCV convention). pyrender wants the forward direction to be **−z**, hence the black frames unless we flip.

---

If you want an extra sanity check after the fix: set `scene.bg_color=[0.2,0.2,0.2]` so “nothing rendered” looks gray instead of black, and/or render depth once (nonzero depth confirms geometry is in view).

## 1) Patch `mouse_sim.py`: export cage into the same JSON

### A) Change the export function to include cage
Modify your `export_cameras_json(...)` to take cage dimensions too and include them:

```python
def export_scene_json(cams, path: str, cage_width: float, cage_depth: float, cage_height: float) -> None:
    data = {
        "cage": {
            "origin": [0.0, 0.0, 0.0],
            "width": float(cage_width),
            "depth": float(cage_depth),
            "height": float(cage_height),
        },
        "cameras": []
    }
    for cam in cams:
        data["cameras"].append({
            "name": cam.name,
            "width": cam.width,
            "height": cam.height,
            "fx": float(cam.fx),
            "fy": float(cam.fy),
            "cx": float(cam.cx),
            "cy": float(cam.cy),
            # world -> camera: Pc = R*Pw + t   (CV convention)
            "R": cam.R.tolist(),
            "t": cam.t.tolist(),
            "pos_world": cam.pos_world.tolist(),
        })
    with open(path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        json.dump(data, f, indent=2)
```

### B) Call it from `simulate()` (or wherever you create cams)
Replace the old call with:

```python
if args.export_cameras:
    scene_path = os.path.join(args.out_dir, "cameras.json")
    export_scene_json(cams, scene_path, args.cage_width, args.cage_depth, args.cage_height)
```

Now `out-dir/cameras.json` contains everything `mouse_deform_render.py` needs.

## 2) Extend `mouse_deform_render.py` with cage face textures

### A) Add CLI args
In `argparse` add:

```python
ap.add_argument("--T", default=None, help="Top face image (z=height)")
ap.add_argument("--B", default=None, help="Bottom face image (z=0)")
ap.add_argument("--N", default=None, help="North wall image (y=depth)")
ap.add_argument("--S", default=None, help="South wall image (y=0)")
ap.add_argument("--E", default=None, help="East wall image (x=width)")
ap.add_argument("--W", default=None, help="West wall image (x=0)")
ap.add_argument("--cage-alpha", type=float, default=1.0, help="Face opacity 0..1")
```

### B) Read cage from JSON
Change your loader so it returns both cameras + cage:

```python
def load_scene_json(path: str):
    with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        data = json.load(f)

    cage = data.get("cage", None)
    cams = []
    for c in data["cameras"]:
        cams.append(CameraSpec(...))  # as before
    return cage, cams
```

Then in `main()`:

```python
cage, cams = load_scene_json(args.cameras)
```

### C) Build a textured cage once (not per frame)
Add these helper functions (uses `trimesh` + `Pillow`, which you already have):

```python
from PIL import Image
import trimesh
import pyrender
import numpy as np

def _load_img(path: str | None):
    if not path:
        return None
    img = Image.open(path).convert("RGBA")
    return img

def make_textured_quad(p00, p10, p11, p01, img_rgba, alpha=1.0):
    """
    Quad corners in CCW order as seen from the *inside* of the cage.
    UVs map image onto the quad.
    """
    vertices = np.array([p00, p10, p11, p01], dtype=np.float64)
    faces = np.array([[0, 1, 2], [0, 2, 3]], dtype=np.int64)
    uv = np.array([[0, 0], [1, 0], [1, 1], [0, 1]], dtype=np.float64)

    if img_rgba is None:
        # fallback constant color if no image is provided
        color = np.ones((4,), dtype=np.uint8) * 255
        visual = trimesh.visual.ColorVisuals(vertex_colors=np.tile(color, (4, 1)))
    else:
        if alpha < 1.0:
            arr = np.array(img_rgba, dtype=np.uint8)
            arr[..., 3] = (arr[..., 3].astype(np.float32) * alpha).clip(0, 255).astype(np.uint8)
            img_rgba = Image.fromarray(arr, mode="RGBA")

        material = trimesh.visual.material.SimpleMaterial(image=img_rgba)
        visual = trimesh.visual.texture.TextureVisuals(uv=uv, image=img_rgba, material=material)

    m = trimesh.Trimesh(vertices=vertices, faces=faces, visual=visual, process=False)
    return pyrender.Mesh.from_trimesh(m, smooth=False)

def add_cage_to_scene(scene: pyrender.Scene, cage: dict, tex: dict, alpha: float):
    """
    Cage coordinate system:
      x in [0,width], y in [0,depth], z in [0,height]
    Face naming:
      S: y=0, N: y=depth, W: x=0, E: x=width, B: z=0, T: z=height
    We orient quads so they are visible from inside the cage.
    """
    w = float(cage["width"]); d = float(cage["depth"]); h = float(cage["height"])

    imgs = {k: _load_img(tex.get(k)) for k in ["T","B","N","S","E","W"]}

    # Bottom (z=0), viewed from inside means normal +z
    scene.add(make_textured_quad(
        [0, 0, 0], [w, 0, 0], [w, d, 0], [0, d, 0], imgs["B"], alpha
    ))

    # Top (z=h), viewed from inside means normal -z (reverse order)
    scene.add(make_textured_quad(
        [0, d, h], [w, d, h], [w, 0, h], [0, 0, h], imgs["T"], alpha
    ))

    # South wall (y=0), inside normal +y
    scene.add(make_textured_quad(
        [0, 0, 0], [w, 0, 0], [w, 0, h], [0, 0, h], imgs["S"], alpha
    ))

    # North wall (y=d), inside normal -y (reverse)
    scene.add(make_textured_quad(
        [0, d, h], [w, d, h], [w, d, 0], [0, d, 0], imgs["N"], alpha
    ))

    # West wall (x=0), inside normal +x
    scene.add(make_textured_quad(
        [0, d, 0], [0, 0, 0], [0, 0, h], [0, d, h], imgs["W"], alpha
    ))

    # East wall (x=w), inside normal -x (reverse)
    scene.add(make_textured_quad(
        [w, d, h], [w, 0, h], [w, 0, 0], [w, d, 0], imgs["E"], alpha
    ))
```

### D) Attach the cage to every camera scene at setup time
In your per-camera scene creation loop, after you create `scene`:

```python
if cage is not None:
    tex = {"T": args.T, "B": args.B, "N": args.N, "S": args.S, "E": args.E, "W": args.W}
    add_cage_to_scene(scene, cage, tex, alpha=args.cage_alpha)
    # also set a non-black bg just in case
    scene.bg_color = [30, 30, 30]
```

Because the cage is static, this is done once and costs nothing per frame.

---

## 3) Why “warp” is easy here
For axis-aligned cage walls, you don’t need any special warping. The images are mapped via UVs onto planar rectangles. If you later want “fit image without stretching”, you can add a mode that letterboxes in UV-space, but that’s optional.

## One more practical note
If any of your JPEGs are dark and you rely on lighting to see them: textures are multiplied by lighting in most renderers. If you want the cage to look like an “emissive photo box” (always bright), we can swap the cage materials to an unlit/emissive style. With `pyrender` that’s a little fiddly but doable; the simplest workaround is stronger ambient light:

```python
scene.ambient_light = [0.8, 0.8, 0.8]
```

Assistant: Yes — that’s exactly the right place and shape for it.

A couple of small corrections / gotchas to make it reliably work:

### 1) `scene.bg_color` expects 0..255 *or* 0..1 depending on version
`pyrender.Scene(bg_color=...)` is usually **0–255 uint8-like**. Your `[30,30,30]` is fine. (If you ever see weird colors, switch to `[0.12,0.12,0.12]`.)

### 2) `scene.ambient_light` should be a float RGB in 0..1
Your `scene.ambient_light = [0.8,0.8,0.8]` is correct (brightens textures).

### 3) Make sure the cage is added **after** the camera node is added (not required, but cleaner)
Your `make_scene_for_camera(cam)` already adds the camera + lights. Adding cage right after is good.

### 4) The cage should be visible from inside: winding order matters
The `add_cage_to_scene(...)` I gave uses vertex ordering so the faces are visible from inside the cage. If you still don’t see the cage, it’s likely **back-face culling**. Quick test:
- render once with `RenderFlags.SKIP_CULL_FACES` (same trick as with the mouse mesh)

```python
from pyrender import RenderFlags
color, _ = renderer.render(scene, flags=RenderFlags.SKIP_CULL_FACES)
```

If that fixes it, then either keep that flag, or reverse the vertex order for the offending faces.

Assistant: That traceback is 100% caused by a **placeholder left in your `load_scene_json()`**:

```python
cams.append(CameraSpec(...))  # as before
```

`...` is literally being passed to the constructor, so Python can’t supply the required args.

### Fix: implement `load_scene_json()` properly (and keep it backward-compatible)

Drop this into `mouse_deform_render.py`, replacing your current `load_scene_json` (and you can delete the old `load_cameras_json` if you want):

```python
def load_scene_json(path: str):
    """
    Supports both:
      (new) {"cage": {...}, "cameras": [...]}
      (old) {"cameras": [...]}   (no cage)
    Returns: (cage_dict_or_None, list[CameraSpec])
    """
    if not os.path.exists(path):
        raise FileNotFoundError(path)

    with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        data = json.load(f)

    cage = data.get("cage", None)

    cam_list = data.get("cameras", None)
    if cam_list is None:
        raise ValueError("JSON must contain key 'cameras'")

    cams: List[CameraSpec] = []
    for c in cam_list:
        cams.append(CameraSpec(
            name=c["name"],
            width=int(c["width"]),
            height=int(c["height"]),
            fx=float(c["fx"]),
            fy=float(c["fy"]),
            cx=float(c["cx"]),
            cy=float(c["cy"]),
            R_wc=np.array(c["R"], dtype=np.float64),
            t_wc=np.array(c["t"], dtype=np.float64),
        ))

    if not cams:
        raise ValueError("No cameras found in JSON")

    return cage, cams
```

Then in `main()` use:

```python
cage, cams = load_scene_json(args.cameras)
```

That alone fixes your crash.

If you paste the first ~20 lines of your actual `out3mesh/cameras.json` (just the JSON structure, not everything), I can tell you immediately whether it already contains `"cage"` and whether your loader needs any additional robustness.

User: Thanks and sorry for missing to replace the "...".

The cage scene has a couple of flaws. It seems like the front camera sees the south wall in front of the cage with the mouse moving inside of it. The top camera is not occluded by the top ceiling; but it does not show the perspectively distorted side walls N,E,S,W. The side cam suffers from the same problem as the front cam.

In the videos from mouse_sim.py you plot the walls by showing the cube outline lines of the cage. These distorted rectangels need  to be filled by the images. Do not care for transform details. Just fit the rectangular image to the distorted quadrangle. The trick is that out of the six images each cam sees only 5, as the wall the cam looks through is not allowed to be rendered.

Assistant: Yes — the symptoms match two concrete issues in the cage implementation:

1) **You rendered all 6 walls for every camera**, so the “through-wall” (the one between camera and interior) blocks the view and looks like the mouse is “behind a poster”.  
2) **Your cage faces were oriented for inside viewing only**, so from an outside camera (especially the top camera) some walls can disappear due to back-face culling — which is why you don’t see the side walls as perspective-distorted quads.

The good news: you don’t need any fancy “2D warp”. If you render each wall as a 3D quad with UVs, the perspective projection automatically maps the rectangular image to the distorted quadrilateral, exactly like the cube outline in `mouse_sim.py`—just filled.

Below is a robust fix: **for each camera, render only 5 faces** (skip the face the camera looks through) and make cage faces **double-sided** (or disable culling).

---

## 1) Compute which cage face to skip per camera

Use the camera **position** and **view direction** (in world coordinates) derived from the stored world→cam extrinsics in CV convention:

- camera center: `C = -R.T @ t`
- forward direction (CV): `dir = R.T @ [0,0,1]`  (camera +z forward)

Then intersect the ray `C + s*dir` with the six axis-aligned planes and pick the nearest valid hit.

Add this to `mouse_deform_render.py`:

```python
def camera_center_world(R_wc: np.ndarray, t_wc: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
    return -R_wc.T @ t_wc

def camera_forward_world_cv(R_wc: np.ndarray) -> np.ndarray:
    # In CV convention, camera looks along +Z in camera coords.
    return R_wc.T @ np.array([0.0, 0.0, 1.0], dtype=np.float64)

def pick_face_to_skip(C: np.ndarray, d: np.ndarray, cage: dict, eps: float = 1e-9) -> str | None:
    """
    Returns one of: 'T','B','N','S','E','W' to skip, or None.
    Cage coords: x in [0,w], y in [0,dep], z in [0,h]
    """
    w = float(cage["width"])
    dep = float(cage["depth"])
    h = float(cage["height"])

    best = (np.inf, None)

    def consider(face: str, s: float, P: np.ndarray):
        nonlocal best
        if s <= eps:
            return
        x, y, z = P
        if face in ("E", "W"):
            if (0 - eps) <= y <= (dep + eps) and (0 - eps) <= z <= (h + eps):
                best = min(best, (s, face))
        elif face in ("N", "S"):
            if (0 - eps) <= x <= (w + eps) and (0 - eps) <= z <= (h + eps):
                best = min(best, (s, face))
        elif face in ("T", "B"):
            if (0 - eps) <= x <= (w + eps) and (0 - eps) <= y <= (dep + eps):
                best = min(best, (s, face))

    # planes: x=0(W), x=w(E), y=0(S), y=dep(N), z=0(B), z=h(T)
    if abs(d[0]) > eps:
        s = (0.0 - C[0]) / d[0]
        consider("W", s, C + s * d)
        s = (w - C[0]) / d[0]
        consider("E", s, C + s * d)

    if abs(d[1]) > eps:
        s = (0.0 - C[1]) / d[1]
        consider("S", s, C + s * d)
        s = (dep - C[1]) / d[1]
        consider("N", s, C + s * d)

    if abs(d[2]) > eps:
        s = (0.0 - C[2]) / d[2]
        consider("B", s, C + s * d)
        s = (h - C[2]) / d[2]
        consider("T", s, C + s * d)

    return best[1]
```

This implements your “trick”: each camera gets exactly one face removed — the one it looks through.

---

## 2) Make cage quads double-sided (fix missing walls in top view)

Modify your quad builder so triangles exist in both windings (double-sided), so you don’t depend on culling flags:

```python
def make_textured_quad(p00, p10, p11, p01, img_rgba, alpha=1.0):
    vertices = np.array([p00, p10, p11, p01], dtype=np.float64)

    # Two-sided: add reversed faces too
    faces = np.array([
        [0, 1, 2], [0, 2, 3],
        [2, 1, 0], [3, 2, 0],
    ], dtype=np.int64)

    uv = np.array([[0, 0], [1, 0], [1, 1], [0, 1]], dtype=np.float64)

    if img_rgba is None:
        color = np.array([255, 255, 255, 255], dtype=np.uint8)
        visual = trimesh.visual.ColorVisuals(vertex_colors=np.tile(color, (4, 1)))
        m = trimesh.Trimesh(vertices=vertices, faces=faces, visual=visual, process=False)
        return pyrender.Mesh.from_trimesh(m, smooth=False)

    if alpha < 1.0:
        arr = np.array(img_rgba, dtype=np.uint8)
        arr[..., 3] = (arr[..., 3].astype(np.float32) * alpha).clip(0, 255).astype(np.uint8)
        img_rgba = Image.fromarray(arr, mode="RGBA")

    material = trimesh.visual.material.SimpleMaterial(image=img_rgba)
    visual = trimesh.visual.texture.TextureVisuals(uv=uv, image=img_rgba, material=material)
    m = trimesh.Trimesh(vertices=vertices, faces=faces, visual=visual, process=False)
    return pyrender.Mesh.from_trimesh(m, smooth=False)
```

Now the side walls will show up in the top camera as perspective-distorted quads (thin strips if the camera is nearly orthographic/top-down, but they’ll exist).

---

## 3) Render only the 5 allowed faces for that camera

Change `add_cage_to_scene` to accept `skip_face`:

```python
def add_cage_to_scene(scene: pyrender.Scene, cage: dict, tex: dict, alpha: float, skip_face: str | None):
    w = float(cage["width"]); d = float(cage["depth"]); h = float(cage["height"])
    imgs = {k: _load_img(tex.get(k)) for k in ["T","B","N","S","E","W"]}

    def add(face, p00, p10, p11, p01):
        if skip_face == face:
            return
        scene.add(make_textured_quad(p00, p10, p11, p01, imgs[face], alpha))

    # Define each face as a quad in cage coords (UV mapping happens in make_textured_quad)
    add("B", [0,0,0], [w,0,0], [w,d,0], [0,d,0])
    add("T", [0,0,h], [w,0,h], [w,d,h], [0,d,h])

    add("S", [0,0,0], [w,0,0], [w,0,h], [0,0,h])
    add("N", [0,d,0], [w,d,0], [w,d,h], [0,d,h])

    add("W", [0,0,0], [0,d,0], [0,d,h], [0,0,h])
    add("E", [w,0,0], [w,d,0], [w,d,h], [w,0,h])
```

Note: with the two-sided faces, you don’t need to carefully reverse vertex order anymore.

---

## 4) Apply it in your camera setup loop

This is exactly where your snippet goes, with one extra line to compute `skip_face`:

```python
for cam in cams:
    scene, renderer = make_scene_for_camera(cam)

    if cage is not None:
        Cw = camera_center_world(cam.R_wc, cam.t_wc)
        fw = camera_forward_world_cv(cam.R_wc)
        skip_face = pick_face_to_skip(Cw, fw, cage)

        tex = {"T": args.T, "B": args.B, "N": args.N, "S": args.S, "E": args.E, "W": args.W}
        add_cage_to_scene(scene, cage, tex, alpha=args.cage_alpha, skip_face=skip_face)

        scene.bg_color = [30, 30, 30]
        scene.ambient_light = [0.8, 0.8, 0.8]
```

This fixes:
- front cam: skip `S` (south wall) so it can look “through” it into the cage,
- side cam: skip `E` or `W` depending on its placement,
- top cam: skip `T` (ceiling) so the mouse is visible, while side walls remain visible.

---

## Why this matches your “distorted rectangle fill” request
You’re asking for: project cube edges → get a distorted quadrilateral → fill it with an image.  
That’s exactly what a textured 3D quad does under perspective projection.

No explicit 2D warping code is needed, and you automatically get correct occlusions among remaining faces and the mouse.

---

If you want, I can also suggest one optional refinement: **add a small inward offset** (e.g. `1e-3`) for cage walls to prevent z-fighting at edges, but it’s not required for correctness.

User: I know that it is wrong: But would it be possible to let the mouse always appear in front of the wall images? May be optionally.

Assistant: Yes — and it’s easy to make it an **optional “cheat mode”**.

### What you want (conceptually)
Render the cage normally, then render the mouse again **without letting the cage occlude it**, and composite the mouse pixels on top of the cage pixels.

That guarantees: **mouse always appears in front of wall images**, regardless of true depth.

---

## Minimal robust implementation: 2-pass render + depth-mask composite

### 1) Add a CLI switch
In `mouse_deform_render.py` `argparse`:

```python
ap.add_argument("--mouse-on-top", action="store_true",
                help="Render mouse over cage regardless of depth (non-physical).")
```

### 2) Create TWO scenes per camera at setup time
- `scene_cage`: camera + lights + cage (static)
- `scene_mouse`: camera + lights only (no cage)

The renderer can be the same.

In your setup loop, instead of one scene:

```python

    scene_mouse, _ = make_scene_for_camera(cam)   # but DON'T keep the second renderer
    # (or better: write a make_scene_only(cam) that doesn't create renderer twice)

    # add cage only to scene_cage
```
